Priority in Claiming Lineage of a Foundling
States the rule on whose claim to a foundling's lineage is preferred

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule of priority in claiming a foundling's lineage and explain the rationale of al-anzar (considering the child's benefit).

Core Idea
The free Muslim's claim to a foundling's lineage is preferred over a slave or dhimmi, because the law favors the child's welfare.

When a foundling is claimed by multiple individuals, the law must decide whose claim establishes the child's lineage. This lesson examines the Hanafi rule that prioritizes a free person over a slave and a Muslim over a dhimmi, grounded in the principle of benefiting the child (al-anzar). This is not a fixed hukm taklifi but a rule of tarjih (preference) used to resolve competing claims.

Guided Path
1
State the priority rule
Identify the two pairs given in the text: the free person is more entitled than the slave, and the Muslim is more entitled than the dhimmi. This is a rule of tarjih, not a hukm taklifi. Asserting the lineage (da'wa) of a foundling is a legal claim.
The rule applies when both claimants appear together.
2
Identify the legal rationale
The text explicitly gives the reason: 'tarjihan lima huwa al-anzar fi haqqih' – giving preference to what is more beneficial for the child. This is the Hanafi principle of considering the child's welfare in such matters.
Al-anzar is a recognized basis for tarjih in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Apply the rule to combined scenarios
If a free Muslim claims against a slave dhimmi, the free Muslim is preferred by both criteria. If a free dhimmi claims against a Muslim slave, the two criteria conflict: free over slave vs Muslim over dhimmi. The text does not directly resolve this; in practice, the Hanafi school would weigh the benefit for the child, likely prioritizing freedom over religion because a free parent has full legal capacity.
This step requires understanding that the rule provides two independent comparisons; when they conflict, the principle of al-anzar guides the decision.
4
Recognize the authority and consensus
This ruling comes from the Zahir al-Riwayah and is the mufta bihi position. It is considered muttafaq alayh across the schools, with no intra-Hanafi dispute.
The lack of ikhtilaf reinforces the strength of the reasoning based on child welfare.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْحُرُّ فِي دَعْوَتِهِ اللَّقِيطِ أَوْلَى مِنَ الْعَبْدِ وَالْمُسْلِمُ أَوْلَى مِنَ الذِّمِّيِّ تَرْجِيحًا لِمَا هُوَ الْأَنْظَرُ فِي حَقِّهِ
ترجمہ اور لقیط (بچہ کے نسب) کے بارے میں دعوی کرنے میں اگر غلام و آزاد جمع ہو جائیں تو بہر صورت غلام کے مقابلہ میں آزاد بہتر ہوگا ۔ ( یعنی آزاد شخص سے بچہ کا نسب ثابت کیا جائے گا اور غلام کا دعوی رد کر دیا جائے گا ) ۔ اسی طرح ذمی کے مقابلہ میں مسلم اولی ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس بچہ کے حق میں جو بہتر ہوتا ہے اس کو ترجیح ہوتی ہے (لہذا یہاں بھی آزاد اور مسلم کو بہ نسبت غلام اور ذمی کے ترجیح دی جائے گی )۔
The free person in his claim to the foundling is more entitled than the slave, and the Muslim is more entitled than the dhimmi, giving preference to what is more beneficial for his right. Translation: And regarding the claim of lineage of the foundling, if a slave and a free person both claim, then in any case the free person is better than the slave. (Meaning the lineage of the child will be established from the free person and the slave's claim will be rejected.) Similarly, a Muslim is more entitled than a dhimmi. Because preference is given to what is more beneficial for this child (so here the free and Muslim are preferred over the slave and dhimmi).
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage states a ruling on who has priority in claiming the lineage of a foundling when multiple claimants appear. The Hanafi school holds that if a free person and a slave both claim the child, the free person's claim is accepted and the slave's is rejected. Similarly, if a Muslim and a dhimmi (non-Muslim subject) both claim, the Muslim's claim is preferred. The reason is that the law gives preference to what is more beneficial for the child (al-anzar fi haqqihi). Being raised by a free Muslim is more advantageous for the child's well-being and future. This ruling is based on the legal principle of considering the child's best interest, which is a recognized basis for preference (tarjih) in the Hanafi school. The Urdu commentary clarifies that this preference applies in all cases when both claimants appear together.

Key Terms
لقیط (laqīṭ): A child found abandoned whose lineage is unknown.
دعوته (da‘watuhu): His claim to the lineage of the child.
أولى (awlā): More entitled or preferred in legal priority.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a free Muslim and a slave dhimmi both claim a foundling, whose claim is given priority according to Hanafi fiqh?
A) The free Muslim
B) The slave dhimmi
C) Both are equal
D) No one's claim is accepted

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prioritizes a free Muslim's claim to a foundling over a slave or dhimmi, based on the principle of al-anzar (considering the child's best interest).

Property Found Tied to the Foundling Belongs to Him
Ruling on ownership and disposal of property found with a foundling.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on property found tied to a foundling, distinguishing between the relied-upon position (with qadi's permission) and the divergent opinion.

Core Idea
Physical attachment to a foundling indicates ownership, but disposal requires qadi's oversight.

When a foundling is discovered with property physically tied to him or to his mount, the Hanafi school presumes the property is his. However, who may spend this property and under what authority? This passage from Al-Hidayah explains the ruling and presents a difference within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
The property belongs to the foundling, based on the apparent state (al-zahir) of physical attachment.
This is the core principle: consideration of the external appearance when no contrary evidence exists.
2
Understand the finder's role
The finder (wajid) is to spend the property on the foundling, but generally must seek the qadi's permission because the property is considered lost (mal da'i') and the qadi has general guardianship over foundlings.
3
Note the internal ikhtilaf
Some Hanafi scholars said (qila) that the finder may spend without qadi's permission, relying on the apparent ownership of the child.
This is a weaker opinion within the school.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is with qadi's permission, as Al-Hidayah presents it as the main ruling and labels the alternative as 'qila'.
This is the position from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ وُجِدَ مَعَ اللَّقِيطِ مَالٌ مَشْدُودٌ عَلَيْهِ فَهُوَ لَهُ اعْتِبَارًا بِالظَّاهِرِ وَكَذَا إِذَا كَانَ مَشْدُودًا عَلَى دَابَّةٍ وَهُوَ عَلَيْهَا لِمَا ذَكَرْنَا ثُمَّ يَصْرِفُهُ الْوَاجِدُ إِلَيْهِ بِأَمْرِ الْقَاضِي لِأَنَّهُ مَالٌ ضَائِعٌ وَلِلْقَاضِي وِلَايَةُ صَرْفِ مِثْلِهِ إِلَيْهِ وَقِيلَ يَصْرِفُهُ بِغَيْرِ أَمْرِ الْقَاضِي لِأَنَّهُ اللَّقِيطُ ظَاهِرًا
ترجمہ اور لقیط کے ساتھ اس سے بندھا ہوا کچھ مال بھی موجود ہو تو وہ مال بھی اس بچہ کا ہوگا ۔ اسی طرح اگر یہ مال ایسے جانور پر بندھا ہوا ہو جس پر وہ بچہ (لقیط) پایا گیا ہے تو وہ مال بھی اس بچہ کا ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ظاہری حالت اس کی شاہد ہے ۔ پھر جس شخص نے بچہ اور اس کے ساتھ مال کو پایا ہے وہی قاضی کی اجازت سے اس مال کو اسی بچہ پر خرچ کرے۔ کیونکہ اس مال کا دوسرا کوئی مالک و حافظ نہیں ہے اور ایسے مال کو لقیط پر خرچ کرنے کا اختیار صرف قاضی کو ہوتا ہے اور بعضوں نے کہا ہے کہ قاضی کے حکم کے بغیر بھی یہ خرچ کر سکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ بظاہر یہ مال اسی لقیط کا ہے۔
And if property is found with the foundling, tied on him, then it is his, based on the apparent state. Likewise if it is tied on an animal and he is upon it, for what we mentioned. Then the finder spends it on him by order of the qadi because it is lost property, and the qadi has authority to spend its like on him. And it is said that he spends it without the order of the qadi because it is apparently the foundling's. Translation: And if some property is found tied to the foundling, then that property also belongs to the child. Similarly if this property is tied on an animal on which the foundling was found, then that property also belongs to the child. Because the apparent state is evidence. Then the person who found the child and the property spends that property on the child with the permission of the qadi, because this property has no other owner or caretaker, and only the qadi has authority to spend such property on the foundling. And some have said that he can spend without the qadi's order, because apparently this property belongs to the foundling.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage rules on property found physically attached to a foundling. The Hanafi school holds that if property is tied to the child or to an animal on which the child is found, that property is considered the child's own. This is based on the apparent state (al-zahir) — the physical attachment indicates ownership. The finder (al-wajid) is then responsible for spending this property on the foundling, but he must do so with the qadi's permission. The reason is that the property is considered lost (mal da'i‘) and only the qadi has guardianship (wilaya) to dispose of such property on behalf of the foundling. However, there is a divergent opinion (qila) that the finder may spend it without the qadi's order, because the apparent state already indicates the property belongs to the foundling. This ikhtilaf reflects a tension between the need for judicial oversight and the practical benefit of immediate expenditure.

Key Terms
مشدد عليه (mashdūd ‘alayhi): Tied or attached to the person of the foundling.
واجد (wājid): The person who finds the foundling and the property.
قاضي (qāḍī): The judge with legal authority over the affairs of the foundling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, how must the finder spend property found tied to a foundling?
A) He may spend it freely on the child
B) He must spend it with the permission of the qadi
C) He must give it to the state treasury
D) He cannot spend it at all

Key Takeaway
Property found physically attached to a foundling is his, and the finder must spend it on him with the qadi's permission according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

The Finder's Right to Spend on Necessities
Ruling of permissibility for spending on necessities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that the finder may spend on the foundling's necessities and identify the scope of such spending.

Core Idea
The finder can spend on food and clothing because that is part of maintenance.

This lesson addresses the extent of the finder's authority over the foundling's property. While the finder does not have full guardianship, he is permitted to use the foundling's wealth for essential needs such as food and clothing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
Recognize that the act in question is the finder spending on the foundling's necessities.
2
Understand the ruling
The finder has the authority (wilāyat al-infaq) to spend on indispensable items.
3
Note the examples
The text explicitly mentions food (al-ṭaʿām) and clothing (al-kiswah) as examples.
4
Reason for permissibility
This expenditure is considered part of maintenance (nafaqah), which is the finder's duty towards the foundling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَهُ وِلَايَةُ الْإِنْفَاقِ وَشِرَاءُ مَا لَا بُدَّ لَهُ مِنْهُ كَالطَّعَامِ وَالْكِسْوَةِ لِأَنَّهُ مِنَ الْإِنْفَاقِ لَهُ
ترجمہ اور ملتقط ( پانے والے ) کو یہ حق حاصل ہے کہ نفقہ کے طور پر مال خرچ کرے ۔ ( یعنی اس لقیط کے لئے جن جن چیزوں کی ضرورت ہو ( مثلا کھانا، کپڑا ) کہ یہ چیزیں اس لقیط کے لئے انفاق اور ضروری اخراجات ہیں۔
وَلَا يَجُوزُ تَزْوِيجُ الْمُلْتَقَطِ لِانْعِدَامِ سَبَبِ الْوِلَايَةِ مِنَ الْقَرَابَةِ وَالْمِلْكِ وَالسُّلْطَنَةِ
ترجمہ ۔ لیکن اس بچہ کا اس مال سے نکاح کر دینا جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ نکاح کرانے کے لئے ولی کا ہونا ضروری ہے۔ اور ولی بننے کے لئے سبب ہوتا ہے قریبی رشتہ داری کا ہونا اور مالک ہونا۔ اور حکومت کا ہونا اور اس کے حق میں ان میں سے ایک بات بھی نہیں ہے۔ (اس لئے اگر اس پانے والے نے خود ولی نہ ہونے کے باوجود اس بچہ کا نکاح کر دیا تو جائز نہ ہوگا)۔
And he has authority of spending and purchasing what is indispensable for him, like food and clothing, because that is from spending for him. Translation: And the finder has the right to spend wealth as maintenance. (Meaning for this foundling, whatever is needed, for example food, clothing, these things are maintenance and necessary expenses for this foundling.) And it is not permissible to marry the foundling, due to absence of the cause of guardianship: kinship, ownership, or sovereignty. Translation: But marrying this child from this property is not permissible, because having a guardian is necessary for marriage. And the causes for being a guardian are having close kinship, being an owner, or governmental authority. And in his case none of these exists. (So if the finder marries the child despite not being a guardian, it will not be valid).
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage contains two distinct rulings regarding the finder's (multaqit) authority over the foundling. First, the finder has the right to spend on the foundling's necessities such as food and clothing. This is part of the custodial duty (nafaqah) that the finder undertakes by picking up the child. Second, the finder is expressly prohibited from contracting marriage on behalf of the foundling. The reason is that marriage requires a valid guardian (wali), and the causes of guardianship are three: kinship (qarabah), ownership (milk), or sovereign authority (sultanah). The finder has none of these in relation to the foundling. Therefore, any marriage contract made by the finder would be invalid. This ruling highlights that the finder's authority is limited to care and preservation, not extending to personal status matters like marriage.

Key Terms
ولاية الإنفاق (wilāyat al-infaq): Authority to spend on maintenance and necessities.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on the finder spending on food for the foundling?
A) Not allowed
B) Allowed
C) Obligatory
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
The finder may spend only on necessary maintenance for the foundling, not on extras.

Why the Finder Cannot Marry the Foundling
Ruling of prohibition of marriage by finder.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the prohibition of the finder marrying the foundling and identify the three causes of valid marriage guardianship.

Core Idea
Marriage requires guardianship based on kinship, ownership, or sovereignty; the finder lacks all three.

This lesson explains a key limitation on the finder's authority. The finder cannot contract marriage on behalf of the foundling because he lacks the necessary legal basis for guardianship. Understanding this safeguards the foundling's personal status rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The act is the finder arranging a marriage contract for the foundling.
2
State the ruling
This act is not permissible (lā yajūz).
3
Know the reason
The reason is the absence of a valid cause (sabab) for guardianship.
4
List the three causes
Kinship (qarābah), ownership (milk), and governmental authority (sulṭanah).
5
Apply to the finder
The finder has none of these, so any marriage contract he makes is invalid.

Why the Finder Cannot Trade with Foundling's Property
Ruling with proof via qiyas and rationale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling prohibiting the finder from trading with the foundling's property and identify the two conditions required for authority to engage in profit-oriented disposal.

Core Idea
The finder lacks complete compassion, the mother lacks complete judgment – neither may trade with the child's wealth.

In this lesson, we examine a nuanced ruling from the chapter of luqatah (foundlings). The Hanafi school holds that the person who finds an abandoned child (al-multaqit) is not permitted to engage in commercial transactions with the child's property. This prohibition is derived through qiyas (analogy) with the mother's limited authority over her own child's wealth. The underlying rationale reveals a key principle: the authority to increase wealth requires both sound judgment and genuine compassion. Understanding this reasoning helps clarify the boundary between permissible maintenance and prohibited trading.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State the ruling clearly: the finder cannot dispose of the foundling's property through trade or profit-oriented transactions. Only spending on necessities is allowed.
The term 'tasarrut' here specifically refers to commercial disposal, not all forms of handling.
2
Examine the Analogy (Qiyas)
The ruling is based on qiyas with the mother's position regarding her child's property. In Hanafi fiqh, a mother is not permitted to trade with her child's wealth; she can only spend on necessities. The finder is analogized to the mother.
The asl (original case) is the mother, the far' (new case) is the finder.
3
Extract the Illah (Effective Cause)
Identify the illah: authority to trade for profit requires two qualities – complete sound judgment (al-ra'y al-kamil) and abundant compassion (al-shafaqah al-wafirah). The mother has compassion but deficient judgment; the finder has sound judgment but insufficient compassion. Neither possesses both.
This is a khafiyyah (hidden) illah extracted via tanqih al-manat.
4
Apply the Illah to the New Case
Since the finder lacks full compassion for the foundling, the illah is present (absence of one quality), so the ruling of prohibition applies exactly as in the mother's case.
The absence of either quality prevents the authority to engage in profit-making disposal.
5
Note the Practical Limit
Understand that the prohibition is limited to commercial transactions. The finder is still permitted to spend on the child's necessities (food, clothing, shelter) from the foundling's property. This is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) – the finder acts as a custodian, not an investor.
This restriction protects the foundling's wealth from potential loss.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَلَا تَصَرُّفَهُ فِى مَالِ الْمُلْتَقَطِ اعْتِبَارًا بِالْأُمِّ وَهَذَا لِأَنَّ وِلَايَةَ التَّصَرُّفِ لِتَنْمِيرِ الْمَالِ وَذَلِكَ يَتَحَقَّقُ بِالرَّأْيِ الْكَامِلِ وَالشَّفَقَةِ الْوَافِرَةِ وَالْمَوْجُودُ فِى كُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا أَحَدُهُمَا
ترجمہ کہا اور لقیط (بچہ) کو پانے والا ( ملتقط ) اس بچہ کے مال میں (ضروریات زندگی کے سوا ) تصرف نہیں کر سکتا ہے۔ اس کی مال پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے ۔ یہ اس وجہ سے کہ تصرف کرنے کا حق کسی کو اس لئے دیا جاتا ہے کہ موجود مال کو وہ کسی طرح بڑھائے اور مال کو بڑھانا دو باتوں سے ہوتا ہے۔ (۱) رائے اور مشورے میں وہ کامل درجہ کا ہو (۲) اس کی شفقت بھی بھر پور پائی جارہی ہو حالانکہ اس ملتقط میں ان دو باتوں میں سے صرف ایک بات پائی جاتی ہے ( جیسا کہ ماں کے اندر بھی ایک ہی بات پائی جاتی ہے۔ ( یعنی چھوٹے بچہ کی مال میں پر شفقت تو ہوتی ہے مگر رائے میں وہ ناقص ہوتی ہے۔ اسی طرح لقیط کے مال میں اس کے پانے والے کے اندر اگر چہ رائے کامل ہوتی ہے لیکن اس کی شفقت بچہ پر مکمل نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ اسی لئے وہ اس لقیط کے مال میں خرید وفروخت کرنے کے بارے میں تجارتی اور بڑے پیمانہ پر تصرف نہیں کر سکتا ہے۔
He said: And he has no disposal in the property of the foundling, by analogy with the mother. And this is because the authority of disposal is for increasing the wealth, and that is realized by complete opinion and abundant compassion. And in each one of them only one is found. Translation: He said: And the finder of the foundling child cannot dispose of the child's property (except for necessities) by analogy with the mother. This is because the right of disposal is given so that one can increase the existing wealth, and increasing wealth requires two things: (1) complete soundness of opinion, and (2) abundant compassion. Whereas in the finder only one of these two is found (just as in the mother only one is found. That is, she has compassion for the child's wealth but her opinion is deficient. Similarly, in the finder of the foundling, although his opinion is complete, his compassion for the child is not complete. Therefore he cannot engage in buying and selling or large-scale commercial disposal of the foundling's property.)
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage explains why the finder (multaqit) is not permitted to engage in trade or commercial transactions (tasarrut) with the foundling's property beyond necessities. The ruling is derived by analogy (qiyas) with the mother's position regarding her child's wealth. The basis is that the authority to dispose of property for growth (tanmir al-mal) requires two qualities: complete sound judgment (al-ra'y al-kamil) and abundant compassion (al-shafaqah al-wafirah). The mother has compassion but deficient judgment; the finder has sound judgment but insufficient compassion for the child. Neither possesses both qualities fully, so neither is permitted to trade with the child's property. This istihsan-based ruling protects the foundling's wealth from potential loss due to either poor judgment or lack of genuine concern. The finder's role is limited to basic maintenance, not profit-oriented transactions.

Key Terms
تصرف (taṣarruf): Disposal or transaction, especially commercial buying and selling.
تنمير المال (tanmīr al-māl): Increasing or growing wealth through trade and investment.
ملتقط (multaqit): The finder of a foundling child.
اعتبارا بالأم (i'tibāran bi-l-umm): By analogy with the mother; taking the mother's ruling as the basis.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the finder is not the legal guardian
B) Because the finder lacks either complete judgment or complete compassion
C) Because the foundling owns the property
D) Because trade is risky

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits the finder from trading with the foundling's property because the authority to increase wealth requires both complete judgment and abundant compassion, and the finder lacks the latter.

Finder May Accept Gifts for the Foundling
Ruling that the finder may accept gifts for the foundling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a finder may accept gifts for a foundling, explain why it is a pure benefit, and identify who else shares this authority.

Core Idea
Pure benefit (naf‘ mahd) removes the guardianship barrier: the finder, mother, and executor may all accept gifts for the foundling.

In this lesson, we examine a specific ruling from the Book of Luqatah. The text grants the finder (multaqit) the authority to accept gifts on behalf of the foundling. The key reason is that accepting a gift is a pure benefit — it adds to the child's wealth without any liability. This principle also extends to the child himself (if intelligent), his mother, and her executor. We will unpack the ruling and its implications for guardianship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act the passage permits and its legal classification (permissible). The act is the finder taking possession (qabd) of a gift (hibah) on behalf of the foundling.
The ruling is permissibility (yajuz).
2
Recognize the underlying reason
The text states the reason: 'because it is a pure benefit (naf‘ mahd).' This concept is central to Hanafi guardianship law: acts of pure benefit require less stringent guardianship.
Pure benefit means no liability or detriment to the child.
3
Note other authorized persons
The passage mentions that the minor himself (if intelligent), the mother, and her executor also have this right. This shows that the authority is not exclusive to the finder.
The child's own acceptance requires him to be 'aql (intelligent).
4
Distinguish from risky acts
Acts that involve potential loss or liability (like trade or borrowing) are not pure benefits and require formal guardianship or qadi permission.
The finder cannot engage in risky transactions on behalf of the foundling.
5
Apply the rule to a new scenario
Consider a gift of cash vs. a sale. The finder may accept the cash gift because it is a pure benefit, but cannot conclude a sale because it involves exchange and potential loss.
Always check if the act is a pure benefit first.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَيَجُوزُ أَنْ يُقْبِضَ لَهُ الْهِبَةَ لِأَنَّهُ نَفْعٌ مَحْضٌ وَلِهَذَا يَمْلِكُهُ الصَّغِيرُ بِنَفْسِهِ إِذَا كَانَ عَاقِلًا وَتَمْلِكُهُ الْأُمُّ وَوَصِيُّهَا
ترجمہ اس ملتقط کے لئے یہ بات جائز ہوتی ہے کہ لقیط کے نام پر آئے ہوئے ہبہ کے مال پر قبضہ کرلے اور وصول کر لے ۔ کیونکہ ایسا کرنے میں بچہ کا سراسر فائدہ ہے۔ اسی لئے خود بچہ بھی بشرطیکہ عقل و ہوش کا مالک ہو ایسے مال پر قبضہ کر سکتا ہے۔ اسی طرح بچہ کی ماں اور (وصی) ماں نے جیسے وصیت کر دی ہو سب کو یہ اختیار ہوتا ہے۔
He said: And it is permissible for him to take possession of a gift for him, because it is a pure benefit. And for this reason, a minor who is intelligent can possess it himself, and the mother and her executor can possess it. Translation: It is permissible for the finder to take possession of the gift property that comes for the foundling and receive it, because in doing so there is pure benefit for the child. For this reason, the child himself, if he is intelligent, can take possession of such property. Similarly, the child's mother and the executor (whom she appointed) all have this authority.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage grants the finder (multaqit) the authority to accept gifts (hibah) on behalf of the foundling and take possession (qabd) of them. The reason is that accepting a gift is a pure benefit (naf‘ mahd) for the child — it adds to his wealth without any corresponding liability. The text notes that even the child himself, if he has sufficient intellect, can accept gifts independently. Similarly, the child's mother and any executor she appoints also have this right. This highlights that for acts of pure benefit, the barrier of guardianship is lower, whereas for acts involving risk (like trade) the barrier is higher. The finder's authority here aligns with his role as caretaker, as long as the act is clearly beneficial.

Key Terms
هبة (hibah): A gift, transfer of ownership without compensation.
نفع محض (naf‘ mahḍ): A pure benefit with no detriment or obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, can the finder accept a gift on behalf of the foundling?
A) No, because the finder is not the guardian
B) Yes, because it is a pure benefit
C) Yes, but only with the qadi's permission
D) No, because the foundling's property is under court supervision

Key Takeaway
The finder, mother, and executor may accept gifts for a foundling as long as they are pure benefits, because no guardianship barrier exists for acts that are purely advantageous.

Finder Can Place Foundling in a Craft
Ruling that the finder may teach the foundling a craft for his betterment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling regarding the finder's authority to teach a foundling a craft and explain the basis for this permissibility.

Core Idea
The finder may train the foundling in a craft because it constitutes his upbringing and preservation.

In this lesson, we examine a concise yet significant ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the scope of the finder's (multaqit) authority over a foundling (laqit). While basic care is obligatory, the question arises whether the finder may make long-term educational and vocational decisions. The text affirms that teaching a craft is permitted as part of the child's upbringing (tathqif) and preservation of his well-being (hifz halih).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is the finder allowed to do according to the text? The act is 'yusallimuhu fi sina'ah' – placing the foundling in a craft. The ruling is permissibility (ja'iz / mubah).
The ruling is not an obligation but an authority.
2
Understand the basis
Why is this allowed? The text provides the rationale: 'li-annahu min babi tathqifihi wa hifzi halihi' – because it is from the category of his upbringing and preservation of his condition.
The finder's authority is tied to the child's best interest.
3
Delineate the scope
Does this authority extend to other long-term decisions? By analogy, similar beneficial training (e.g., education, medical care) would also be permitted, as they fall under the same rationale.
The key principle: any action that constitutes tathqif (upbringing) and hifz (preservation) is within the finder's authority.
4
Recognize the legal framework
This ruling fits within the broader category of the finder's responsibilities as a temporary guardian. The finder acts as a guardian ad litem (qayyim) with authority limited to beneficial acts for the child's well-being.
Contrast with decisions like marriage or major financial transactions, which require qadi oversight.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَيُسَلِّمُهُ فِى صِنَاعَةٍ لِأَنَّهُ مِنْ بَابِ تَثْقِيفِهِ وَحِفْظِ حَالِهِ
ترجمہ اور ملتقط کو اس بات کا اختیار ہوتا ہے کہ اس لقیط کو کوئی پیشہ اور ہنر سکھانے میں لگا دے ۔ کیونکہ یہ بات تو اس بچہ کی بہتری اور مستقبل میں حفاظت کی قسموں میں سے ہے ۔ جو اس کے لئے سراسر مفید ہے )
He said: And he may place him in a craft, because it is from the category of his upbringing and preservation of his condition. Translation: And the finder has the authority to engage the foundling in learning a profession and skill, because this is among the types of improvement and future preservation of the child, which is entirely beneficial for him.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage gives the finder the authority to arrange for the foundling to learn a trade or craft (sinā‘ah). This is considered part of the child's upbringing (tathqīf) and preservation of his well-being (hifz hālihi). Teaching a skill enables the child to become self-sufficient in the future, which is clearly in his best interest. The finder's authority here is analogous to that of a parent or guardian in arranging education and vocational training. This ruling underscores that the finder's role extends beyond mere physical care to include preparing the child for independent life.

Key Terms
صناعة (ṣinā‘ah): A craft, trade, or profession taught for livelihood.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, may the finder arrange for the foundling to learn a craft?
A) No, because the finder has no educational authority
B) Yes, because it is part of the child's upbringing and benefit
C) Yes, but only with the qadi's permission
D) No, because the child must choose his own profession

Key Takeaway
Teaching a foundling a craft is a permissible and commendable act of upbringing, rooted in the principle of tathqif and hifz hal.

Luqatah — Found Property

Hiring Out the Foundling: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ijarah of the foundling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on hiring out the foundling, explain the reasoning behind each, and identify the mufta bihi position with its justification.

Core Idea
The finder cannot hire out the foundling because he does not own his benefits — only a guardian like the mother may.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the authority of a foundling's finder (multaqit) to contract the child's labor for wages. The passage from Al-Hidayah reports two views: a permissive view from al-Quduri and a prohibitory view from Al-Jami' al-Saghir. The author of Al-Hidayah declares the latter as the sound (sahih) position. Understanding the basis of each view and the final tarjih is essential for correctly applying the rules of foundling care.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Issue
The core question: May the finder (multaqit) hire out the foundling — i.e., contract his labor for wages (ijarah)?
This is distinct from teaching a craft, which is allowed.
2
Recognize the Two Positions
First position (Quduri): The finder may hire out the child. Second position (Al-Jami' al-Saghir): It is not permissible (la yajuz).
The second position is described as 'sound' (sahih) in the text.
3
Analyze the Reasoning (Wajh)
For permission: Hiring out is a form of upbringing (tathqif) — training the child. For prohibition: The finder does not own the child's benefits (manafi‘); thus consuming them through ijarah is unauthorized.
The prohibition analogizes the finder to a non-guardian, unlike the mother who owns benefits.
4
Examine the Tarjih (Preference)
Al-Marghinani (author of Al-Hidayah) declares the prohibition as the sound position. The decisive factor: ownership of benefits (milk al-manafi‘) is lacking in the finder.
This tarjih is based on the stronger analogy with the mother's exclusive right.
5
Derive the Practical Consequence
If the finder nevertheless hires out the child, the contract is invalid (fasid/batil) according to the relied-upon view. The wages belong to the child, not the finder.
This thamarah al-khilaf affects real cases of foundling care.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَيُوَاجِرَهُ قَالَ الْعَبْدُ الضَّعِيفُ وَهَذَا رِوَايَةُ الْقُدُورِى فِى مُخْتَصَرِهِ وَفِى الْجَامِعِ الصَّغِيرِ لَا يَجُوزُ أَنْ يُوَاجِرَهُ ذَكَرَهُ فِى الْكَرَاهِيَّةِ وَهُوَ لَا صَحُ وَجْهُ الْأَوَّلِ أَنَّهُ يَرْجِعُ إِلَى تَثْقِيفِهِ وَوَجْهُ الثَّانِي أَنَّهُ لَا يَمْلِكُ إِتْلَافَ مَنَافِعِهِ فَاشْتَهَى الْعَمَلَ بِخِلَافِ الْأُمِّ لِأَنَّهَا تَمْلِكُهُ عَلَى مَا نَذْكُرُهُ فِى الْكَرَاهِيَّةِ إِنْ شَاءَ اللهُ تَعَالَى
ترجمہ اور ( قدوری رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے کہا ہے کہ ) اس ملتقط کو اس بات کا بھی اختیار ہوتا ہے کہ اس بچہ (لقیط) کو کرایہ اور مزدوری پر لگا دے۔ اور علامہ عابد الضعیف نے یہی کہا ہے۔ اور یہ قدوری کی اپنی مختصر میں روایت ہے۔ اور جامع صغیر میں ہے کہ اس بچہ کو کرایہ پر لگانا جائز نہیں ہے اس کو کراہیت کے باب میں ذکر کیا ہے اور یہی قول صحیح ہے۔ پہلے قول کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ یہ بھی بچہ کی بہتری اور تعلیم و تربیت ہی کے قبیل سے ہے۔ اور جامع صغیر کی روایت کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ پانے والا بچہ کے منافع کو ختم کرنے کا مالک نہیں ہے اس لئے اس کی اجرت لینا جائز نہیں خلاف ماں کے کہ وہ بچہ کے منافع کی مالک ہوتی ہے جیسا کہ کراہیت کے باب میں ذکر کریں گے ان شاء اللہ تعالیٰ۔
He said: And he may hire him out. Al-'Abd al-Da'if said, and this is the narration of al-Quduri in his Mukhtasar. And in Al-Jami' al-Saghir, it is not permissible to hire him out; he mentioned it in the chapter of karahah, and that is sound. The face of the first is that it goes back to his upbringing. And the face of the second is that he does not own the consumption of his benefits, so he is not like the mother, because she owns it as we will mention in the chapter of karahah, if Allah wills. Translation: And (al-Quduri said that) the finder also has authority to engage the foundling for rent and wages. And 'Allamah al-'Abd al-Da'if said the same. And this is the narration of al-Quduri in his Mukhtasar. And in Al-Jami' al-Saghir, it is not permissible to hire out the child; it is mentioned in the chapter of karahah, and this is the correct statement. The reason for the first opinion is that this is also from the category of the child's betterment and education. And the reason for the narration of Al-Jami' al-Saghir is that the finder does not own the consumption of the child's benefits, so taking his wages is not permissible, unlike the mother, because she owns the child's benefits, as we will mention in the chapter of karahah, if Allah wills.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether the finder can hire out the foundling (i.e., employ him for wages). Two positions are reported. The first, from al-Quduri in his Mukhtasar and supported by al-'Abd al-Da'if, allows it, arguing that hiring out is a form of upbringing (tathqif) and beneficial training. The second, from Al-Jami' al-Saghir (one of the six core books of Imam Muhammad), prohibits it, placing it under karahah (dislike). The author of Al-Hidayah declares this second view to be sahih (sound). The reasoning for prohibition is that the finder does not own the right to consume the child's benefits (manafi‘); that right belongs to someone who has complete guardianship, like the mother who owns her child's benefits. This dispute shows that while teaching a craft is permitted (as in the previous lesson), using the child for commercial labor through ijarah is not allowed according to the relied-upon position, because it involves consuming his benefits, which the finder is not authorized to do.

Key Terms
يؤاجره (yu’ājiruhu): To hire out the foundling, i.e., contract his labor for wages.
الجامع الصغير (al-Jāmi‘ al-Ṣaghīr): One of the six core books (Zahir al-Riwayah) of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.
منافع (manāfi‘): Benefits or usufruct of the child's labor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position in Al-Hidayah, may the finder hire out the foundling?
A) Yes, because it is a form of upbringing
B) No, because the finder does not own the child's benefits
C) Yes, but only with the qadi's permission
D) No, because the child is too young

Key Takeaway
The finder of a foundling cannot hire him out because he lacks ownership of the child's benefits — only a proper guardian like the mother may do so.

Luqatah — Found Property
intermediate
8 min
Ruling on Found Property (Luqata) and Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Guarantee
Intra-Hanafi dispute on liability for luqata without witnesses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the conditions under which luqata is a trust (amanah) vs. guarantee (daman), and identify the positions of Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf when the finder lacks witnesses and the owner disputes his claim.

Core Idea
Found property is trust only when taken with witnesses; without them, the finder is liable if owner denies intent — but Abu Yusuf disagrees.

This passage from Al-Hidayah's commentary clarifies the legal status of found property (luqata) in Hanafi fiqh. It lays out when the finder holds it as a trust (amanah) versus when he becomes liable for compensation (daman). The key point is an intra-Hanafi dispute: what happens if the finder did not make witnesses and the owner later denies his claim of intending to return the item? Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to recognize the role of apparent circumstance (zahir) and the burden of proof in property cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default rule for luqata
The passage first states that luqata is amanah if the finder makes witnesses (ishhad) that he takes it to preserve and return it. Otherwise, if he admits taking for himself, he is liable by consensus.
Making witnesses is the key condition for amanah.
2
Examine the disputed scenario
The dispute arises when the finder did NOT make witnesses, but claims he took it for the owner, while the owner denies this. Is the finder liable if the item is lost?
No witnesses; owner contradicts finder's claim.
3
State Abu Hanifa and Muhammad's position
They hold the finder is liable (yadman) because he admitted to the cause of guarantee (taking another's property) and his claim of intent is not proven. The default assumption is that a person acts for himself.
Liability due to admission of the cause and failure to prove intent.
4
State Abu Yusuf's position and his proof
Abu Yusuf holds the finder is not liable; his word is accepted because the apparent circumstance (zahir) supports him — a Muslim prefers a good deed (hisba) over sin.
Relies on the presumption of good behavior.
5
Analyze the Hanafi response and tarjih
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad counter that the same apparent circumstance could equally suggest the finder acted for himself. Since the finder admitted the act of taking, the burden of proving the mitigating intent falls on him. This view is relied upon for fatwa.
Tarjih: position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ اللُّقَطَةِ
قَالَ اللُّقَطَةُ أَمَانَةً إِذَا أَشْهَدَ الْمُلْتَقِطُ أَنَّهُ يَأْخُذُهَا لِيَحْفَظَهَا وَيَرُدَّهَا عَلَى صَاحِبِهَا لِأَنَّ الْأَخْذَ عَلَى هَذَا الْوَجْهِ مَأْذُونٌ فِيهِ شَرْعًا بَلْ هُوَ الْأَفْضَلُ عِنْدَ عَامَّةِ الْعُلَمَاءِ وَهُوَ الْوَاجِبُ إِذَا خَافَ الصِّيَاعَ عَلَى مَا قَالُوا وَإِذَا كَانَ كَذَلِكَ لَا تَكُونُ مَضْمُونَةً عَلَيْهِ وَكَذَلِكَ إِذَا تَصَادَقَا أَنَّهُ أَخَذَهَا لِلْمَالِكِ لِأَنَّ تَصَادُقَهُمَا حُجَّةٌ حَقِهِمَا فَصَارَ كَالْبَيِّنَةِ وَلَوْ أَقَرَّ أَنَّهُ أَخَذَهُ لِنَفْسِهِ يَضْمَنُ بِالْإِجْمَاعِ لِأَنَّهُ أَخَذَ مَالَ غَيْرِهِ بِغَيْرِ إِذْنِهِ وَبِغَيْرِ إِذْنِ الشَّرْعِ وَإِنْ لَمْ يُشْهِدْ عَلَيْهِ وَقَالَ الْآخِذُ أَخَذْتُهُ لِلْمَالِكِ وَكَذَّبَهُ الْمَالِكُ يَضْمَنُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَمُحَمَّدٍ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ لَا يَضْمَنُ وَالْقَوْلُ قَوْلُهُ لِأَنَّ الظَّاهِرَ شَاهِدٌ لَهُ لِاخْتِيَارِهِ الْحِسْبَةَ دُونَ الْمَعْصِيَّةِ وَلَهُمَا أَنَّهُ أَقَرَّ بِسَبَبِ الضَّمَانِ وَهُوَ أَخْذُ مَالِ الْغَيْرِ وَادَّعَى مَا يُبْرِئُهُ وَهُوَ الْأَخْذُ لِلْمَالِكِ وَفِيهِ وَقَعَ الشَّكُ فَلَا يَبْرَأُ وَمَا ذَكَرَ مِنَ الظَّاهِرِ يُعَارِضُهُ مِثْلَهُ لِأَنَّ الظَّاهِرَ أَنْ يَكُونَ الْمُنْصَرِفُ عَامِلًا لِنَفْسِهِ وَيَكْفِيهِ فِي الْإِشْهَادِ أَنْ يَقُولَ مَنْ سَمِعْتُمُوهُ يُنْشِدُ لُقَطَةً فَدُلُّوهُ عَلَيْهَا وَاحِدَةً كَانَتِ اللُّقَطَةُ أَوْ أَكْثَرَ لِأَنَّهُ اسْمُ جِنْسٍ
ترجمہ ( لقطہ راستہ وغیرہ کا ایسا پڑا ہوا مال جو اٹھا لیا جائے ۔ ) کہا قدوری نے کہ لقطہ اس شخص کے پاس امانت ہے جو اسے اٹھائے بشرطیکہ اس اٹھانے والے (ملتقط ) نے اٹھاتے وقت اس پر کوئی گواہ بھی مقرر کر لیا ہو۔ اس بات پر کہ میں اسے اس لئے اٹھاتا ہوں کہ اس کی حفاظت کروں گا اور مالک سے ملاقات ہو جانے کی صورت میں اسے واپس کر دوں گا۔ کیونکہ اس غرض سے ایسے مال کو اپنی حفاظت میں لے لینے کی شرعاً اجازت ہے ( ۔ کیونکہ حدیث میں ہے کہ جو شخص لقطہ پائے وہ دو عادل گواہ مقرر کر لے۔ رواہ الحق ) ۔ بلکہ عموماً علماء کے نزدیک ایسے مال کو اسی طرح پڑارکھنے سے اسے اٹھا لینا ہی بہتر ہوتا ہے ۔ بلکہ ہمارے مشائخ نے کہا ہے کہ جب اس مال کے ضائع ہو جانے کا خوف ہو تو اسے اٹھا لینا یا لے لینا ہی واجب ہے ) ۔ جیسے ایسی بکری کی جس کے متعلق یہ خطرہ ہو کہ اسے کوئی کتایا بھیٹر یا وغیرہ پکڑ کر کھا جائے گا۔ ایسی صورت میں وہ مال اٹھانے والے کے ذمہ ضمانت کے طور پر نہیں بلکہ امانت کے طور پر ہوگا ( ۔ اس لئے اگر وہ مال ضائع ہو جائے تو اٹھانے والا شخص اس کا ضامن نہیں ہو گا۔ ) اسی طرح اگر خود مالک نے اس ملتقط کے بارے میں تصدیق کرتے ہوئے یہ کہا ہو ( تجربہ کی بناء پر ) کہ اس نے مالک کو پہنچانے کے لئے ہی اسے لیا تھا۔ تو وہ بھی امانت ہی ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ ان دونوں اصل مالک اور اس کے اٹھا لینے والے ) کا آپس میں متفق ہو جانا دونوں کے حق میں دلیل ہے ۔ تو گویا ایسی صورت میں گواہی کے مانند ہو گیا ۔ اور اگر اس اٹھا لینے والے نے اس طرح کا اقرار کیا کہ میں نے تو اسے اپنے لئے لیا تھا۔ تو اس کے ضائع ہو جانے کی صورت میں ) بالا جماع وہ ضامن ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ اس نے غیر کا مال اس کی اجازت کے بغیر اور شرعی اجازت کے بغیر ہی لیا تھا۔ اور اگر لینے والے نے اس کے لیتے وقت اس پر گواہ مقرر نہیں کیا تھا پھر بھی اس نے کہا کہ میں نے تو اسے اس کے مالک کو دینے کے لئے ہی اٹھایا تھا لیکن مالک نے اس منتقط کو جھٹلایا تو امام ابو حنیفہ" و امام محمد کے نزدیک
The Book of Luqata. He said: Luqata is a trust when the finder makes witnesses that he takes it to preserve it and return it to its owner, because taking in this manner is permitted legally; rather it is better according to the generality of scholars, and it is obligatory when he fears loss, as they said. And when it is such, it is not guaranteed against him. Similarly, if both testify that he took it for the owner, because their mutual confirmation is a proof for their right, so it becomes like evidence. And if he admits that he took it for himself, he guarantees by consensus, because he took the property of another without his permission and without legal permission, even if he did not have witnesses against him. And if the taker says 'I took it for the owner' and the owner denies him, he is liable according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: He is not liable, and his statement is accepted because the apparent circumstance supports him due to his choosing good deeds over sin. And for them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) that he admitted to the cause of guarantee, which is taking the property of another, and claimed that which would absolve him, which is taking for the owner, and doubt occurred about that, so he is not absolved. And what he mentioned about the apparent circumstance is countered by its like, because the apparent circumstance is that the person acting is acting for himself. And it suffices for him in making witnesses that he says: 'Whomever you hear announcing a lost item, then guide him to it,' whether the lost item is one or more, because it is a noun of genus.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah (Ashraf ul-Hadaya) discusses the rulings of luqata (found property). It states that luqata is considered a trust (amanah) in the hands of the finder if he takes it with the intention of preserving it and returning it to its owner, and he makes witnesses to that effect. Taking it in this manner is legally permitted (ma'dhun) and is actually better (afdal) according to most scholars. It becomes obligatory (wajib) if the property is likely to be lost (khawf al-diya'). In such cases, the finder is not liable for compensation (daman) if the property is lost. The same rule applies if both the finder and the owner later agree that the finder took it for the owner. However, if the finder admits that he took it for himself, he is liable by consensus (ijma'). The text then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: if the finder did not make witnesses and claims he took it for the owner, but the owner denies this, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that the finder must guarantee (yadman), while Abu Yusuf holds that he does not. Abu Yusuf argues that the apparent circumstance (al-zahir) favors the finder because he chose a praiseworthy act (hisba) over sin. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad counter that the finder admitted to the cause of guarantee (taking another's property) and claimed something that would absolve him (intent for owner), and doubt remains, so he is not absolved. The passage concludes with a note on what suffices for witnessing: the finder can say, 'Whomever you hear announcing a lost item, guide him to it,' whether the item is one or more, because 'luqata' is a noun of genus (ism jins).

Key Terms
لقطة (luqata): Lost property that is picked up or found by someone.
ملتقط (multaqit): The person who finds and picks up the lost property.
أمانة (amanah): A trust; the found property is held as a trust if taken properly, meaning the finder is not liable for accidental loss.
ضمان (daman): Liability to compensate for loss or damage.
إشهاد (ishhad): Making witnesses to attest to the intention of taking the found property for preservation and return.
تصادق (tasaduq): Mutual confirmation between the finder and the owner that the finder took it for the owner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person finds a lost item and takes it without making witnesses, and later the owner disputes his claim that he intended to return it, what is the ruling on the finder's liability?
A) He is not liable because the apparent circumstance supports him.
B) He is liable according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, but not according to Abu Yusuf.
C) He is always liable regardless of his claim.
D) He is never liable because luqata is always a trust.

Key Takeaway
For found property to be a trust (amanah) in the Hanafi school, the finder must make witnesses; otherwise, if the owner disputes, the finder is liable for compensation — this is the relied-upon position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

Luqatah — Found Property
advanced
8 min
Liability of a Finder Without Witnesses: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on liability of finder without witnesses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf on the liability of a finder of lost property when there are no witnesses, and apply the reasoning (talil) to determine the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Admission of taking creates liability; doubt from a later claim does not remove it.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents the default ruling on found property (luqatah) as a trust (amanah) when the finder takes it with witnesses and proper intent. However, the main focus is an intra-Hanafi dispute: when there are no witnesses and the finder claims he took it for the owner, but the owner denies, does the finder become liable? Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say yes; Abu Yusuf says no. Understanding their proofs and the reasoning behind the tarjih will sharpen your ability to handle similar disputes in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
State the default ruling
Identify when luqatah is considered an amanah (trust) and when it becomes dhaman (liable). Note the conditions: witnesses and intention to preserve and return.
The default is amanah with witnesses; without witnesses, the dispute arises.
2
Identify the dispute scenario
Describe the factual scenario: taker has no witnesses, claims he took for owner, owner denies. Recognize that this triggers the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
The key element is the absence of witnesses and conflicting statements.
3
State each imam's position and proof
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold liability (dhaman) because the finder admitted to taking (cause of liability), and his claim of good intent does not remove it. Abu Yusuf holds no liability because apparent circumstances (zahir al-hal) favor the finder's righteousness.
Also note that Maliki, Shafi'i, Hanbali schools agree with Abu Yusuf.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to Abu Yusuf
Understand the counter-argument: apparent circumstances could equally indicate self-interest, so it is not decisive. The admission of taking is stronger evidence.
This is the talil (reasoning) that leads to the preference for Abu Hanifa's view.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical consequence
The position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is adopted for fatwa due to its strength and alignment with qiyas. The practical consequence: in a court case, the finder may be held liable if he has no witnesses, even if he claims good intent.
This illustrates the thamarah al-khilaf.

كتاب اللقطة
قَالَ اللُّقْطَهُ أمَانَةً إِذَا أَشْهَدَ الْمُلْتَقِطْ أَنَّهُ يَأْخُذُهَا لِيَحْفَظْهَا وَيَرُدَّهَا عَلَى صَاحِبَهَا لِأَنَّ الْأخْذَ عَلَى هَذَا الْوَجْهِ مَأْذُونَ فِيهِ شَرْعَابَلْ هُوَ الأَفْضَلُ عِنْدَ عَامَّةِ الْعُلَمَاءِ وَهُوَ الْوَاجِبُ إذَا خَافَ الصِّيَاعَ عَلَى مَا قَالُو اَوَإِذَا كَانَ كَذَالِكَ لَا تَكُونُ مَضْمُونَةً عَلَيْهِ وَكَذَالِكَ إِذَا تَصَادَقَا أَنَّهُ أَخَذَهَا لِلْمَالِكِ لِأَنَّ تَصَادِقُهُمَا حُجَّةٌ حَقِهِمَا فَصَارَ كَالْبَيِّنَةِ وَلَوْ أَفَرَأَنَّهُ أَخَذَهُ لِنَفْسِهِ يَضْمَنُ بِالَّا جُمَاعِ لِأَنَّهُ أَحَدَ مَالَ غَيْرِهِ بِغَيْرِ إِذْنِهِ وَبِغَيْرِ إِذْنِ الشَّرْعِ وَإِنَّ لَمْ الشُّهُودَ عَلَيْهِ وَقَالَ الْآخِذُ  َأخَذْتُهُ لِلْمَالِكِ وَكَذَّبَهُ الْمَالِكِ يَضَمَنُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَة وَمُحَمَّد وَقَالَ أَبُويُوسُف لَا يَضْمَن وَالْقَوْلُ قَوْلُهُ لأَنَّ الظَّاهِرَ شَاهِدُ لَهُ لا خُتِيارِهِ الْحِسْبَةِ دُونَ الْمَعْصِيَّةِ وَلَهُمَا أَنَّهُ أَقَرَّ بِسَبَبِ الضَّمَانِ وَهُوَ اُخْدِمَالِ الْغَيْرِ وَادَّعَى مَايُبرِئُهُ وَهُوَ الْأَخَذُ لِمَالِكِ، وَفِيهِ وَقَعَ الشَّكُ فَلاَيْرَأُ وَمَا ذَكَرَ مِنَ الظَّاهِرِ يُعَارِضُهُ مِثْلَهُ لِأَنَّ الظَّاهِرَأنْ يَكُونَ الْمُنصَرِفُ عَامِلًا لِنَفْسِهِ وَيَكْفِيهِ فِى الْإِشَهَادَ أَنْ يَقُوْلَ مَنْ سَمِعْتُمُوهُ يُنْشِدَ لُقْطَةٌ فَدَلُّوهُ عَلَى وَاحِدَةً كَانَتِ اللَّقْطَة أو اكثر لأَنَّهُ إِسم جنس

معلوم ہونی چاہئے کہ یہ حکم عام ہے کہ خواہ لقطہ ایک ہو یا ایک سے زیادہ ہو کیونکہ لقطہ اسم جنس ہے۔ لیکن ملتقط کو چاہئے کہ اس چیز کی شناخت کر دے)
Translation: The Book of Luqatah. The nature of luqatah. He said: The found item is a trust when the finder makes witnesses that he takes it to preserve it and return it to its owner, because taking in this manner is permitted by Shari'ah, rather it is preferable according to most scholars, and it is obligatory when fear of loss, as they said. And if that is the case, it is not guaranteed (dhaman) upon him. Likewise, if they mutually agree that he took it for the owner, because their mutual agreement is a proof for both, so it becomes like evidence. If he declares that he took it for himself, he is liable by consensus, because he took another's property without his permission and without legal permission. If there are no witnesses upon him, and the taker said "I took it for the owner" but the owner denies, then according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad he is liable, and Abu Yusuf said he is not liable, and his statement is accepted because apparent circumstances witness for him—he chose righteousness over sin. Their (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad's) proof is that he admitted to the cause of liability, which is taking another's property, and claimed what would exonerate him, which is taking for the owner, and doubt arose, so it does not remove (liability). What he mentioned about apparent circumstances is countered by a similar appearance: that normally a person acts for himself. And it suffices for making witnesses that he say: 'Whoever you hear announcing a lost item, direct them to me,' whether the item is one or more, because it is a generic noun.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage is an intra-madhhab dispute on the liability of a finder (multaqit) of lost property. It begins by stating the default ruling: if the finder takes the item with witnesses and the intention to preserve and return it, it is an amanah (trust) not dhaman (guaranteed). The text also notes that taking it is preferable, and even obligatory if there is fear of loss. However, the core dispute arises when there are no witnesses and the finder claims he took it for the owner, but the owner denies. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that the finder is liable (dhamin) because he admitted to the act of taking another's property, which is the cause of liability, and his claim of good intention is not enough to remove that liability. Abu Yusuf disagrees, ruling that the finder is not liable because the apparent circumstance (zahir al-hal) supports him—he would naturally choose a righteous act (helping the owner) over sin (taking for himself). Abu Yusuf also gives the finder the benefit of the doubt (qawl qawluhu). The passage then explains the counter-argument: the same apparent circumstance could equally suggest that a person acts for himself, creating doubt. Finally, it clarifies that for witnesses, it is enough to announce generally without specifying the item.

Key Terms
اللقطة (al-luqatah): Lost or discarded property (including goods, animals) that is found and taken possession of by a finder
الملتقط (al-multaqit): The person who picks up and takes possession of luqatah
الضمان (al-dhaman): Liability to compensate if the item is lost or destroyed
الأمانة (al-amanah): A trust: the finder is not liable for loss if he was not negligent
الإشهاد (al-ishhad): Making witnesses (at the time of taking) to establish the act of taking for preservation

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, why is the finder liable even if he claims he took the lost item for the owner?
A) Because the finder did not make witnesses.
B) Because the finder admitted to taking the property, which is the cause of liability, and the claim of good intent does not remove doubt.
C) Because the item was valuable.
D) Because the owner denied the finder's claim.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the finder of lost property is liable if he takes it without witnesses and the owner denies his claim of good intent, because the admission of taking creates a liability that is not removed by a doubtful claim.

Module 18 · Lesson 28

Luqatah — Found Property
intermediate
10 min
Announcement Period for Lost Property
Ruling on duration of announcing found property based on value, with intra-Hanafi views and hadith proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the duration of announcement for found property, distinguish between the intra-Hanafi views, and apply the hadith to derive the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
The finder must announce found property for one year — the hadith and Zahir al-Riwayah prevail over value-based distinctions.

When someone finds a valuable item, they have a responsibility to try to return it to its owner. This lesson clarifies how long the finder must publicly announce the found property according to the Hanafi school. The source passage presents a difference of opinion within the school, and we will see why the one-year rule for all items becomes the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is ta'rif (announcement/identifying) of found property (luqatah). The ruling is that it is wajib (obligatory).
Wajib here means obligatory under the Hanafi definition: omission is sin but act is valid if done later.
2
Locate the matn position
The matn (Quduri) states that if the item is less than 10 dirhams, announce for a few days; if 10 dirhams or more, announce for a year. This is one riwayah from Abu Hanifa.
This view uses qiyas on theft and mahr thresholds.
3
Identify the Zahir al-Riwayah position
Muhammad al-Shaybani in al-Asl (Zahir al-Riwayah) requires one year for all items regardless of value, supported by another riwayah from Abu Hanifa and the hadith.
This is the position of Malik and Shafi'i as well.
4
Analyze the dalil
The hadith: 'Whoever picks up something, let him announce it for a year.' In Hanafi usul, the imperative indicates obligation (wujub). The explicit duration 'sanan' (year) sets the time limit.
The hadith is the strongest proof; no evidence overrides it.
5
Apply tarjih and determine mufta bihi
The one-year rule is taken because the hadith is direct and the madhhab hierarchy places Zahir al-Riwayah over individual riwayat. Thus, the mufta bihi for fatwa is one year for all items.
Precaution (ihtiyat) also supports the longer duration.

لقطہ کا اعلان کتنے دن تک کیا جائے گا
قَالَ فَإِنْ كَانَتْ أَقَلَّ مِنْ عَشَرَةِ دَرَاهِمَ عَرَّفَهَا أَيَّا مَا وَإنْ كَانَتْ عَشَرَةً فَصَا عِدًا عَرَّفَهَا حَوْلًا قَالَ الْعَبْدُالضَّعِيفُ وَ هذِهِ رِوَايَةٌ عَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَة وَقَوْلُهُ أَيَّامًا مَعْنَاهُ عَلَى حَسَبِ مَا يَرَى الْإِمَامُ وَقَدَّرَهُ مُحَمَّدُ فِي الْأَصْلِ بِالْحَوْلِ عَنْ غَيْر تَفصيل بَيْسَ الْقِلِيل وَالكَثيرِ وَهُوَ قَوْلُ مَالِكَ وَالشَّافِعِى لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامِ مَنِ الْتَقَطَ شَيَا فَلْيُعَرِفَهُ سَنَةً مِنْ فضل وَجْهُ الأَوَّلِ أَنَّ التَّقْدِيرَ بِالْحَوْلِ وَرَدَ فِي لُقْطَهُ كَانَتْ مِائَةَ دِينَارٍ تُسَاوِي أَلْفَ دِرْهَم وَالْعَشَرَهُ وَمَا فَوْقَهَا فِي مَعْنِ الألْفِ فِى تَعَلَّقِ القَطع به فِى السَّرَقَهُ وَتَعَلَّقِ اسْتِحْلَالِ الفَرْج بِهِ وَلَيْسَتْ فِى مَعَنَاهَا فِي حَقِّ تَعَلَّق الزَّكوةِ فَأَوْجَبْنَا التَّعْرِيفَ بِالْحَوِّلِ اِحْتِيَاطًا وَمَادُونَ الْعَشَرَةِ لَيْسَ فِي مَعْنَى الْأَلْفِ بِوَجْهِ مَّا فَفَوَّ ضُنَا إِلَى رَأْيِ الْمُبْتَلَى بِهِ وَقِيلَ الصَّحِيحُ أَنَّ شَنْيا مِنْ هَذِهِ الْمَقَادِيرِ لَيْسَ بِلَازِمٍ وَيُفَوِّضُ إِلى رَأَى الْمُتَّقِطِ يُعَرِّفُهَا إِلَى أَنْ تَعْلِبَ عَلَى طَيْهِ أَنَّ صَاحِبَهَا لَا يَطْلُبُهَا بَعْدَ ذَالِكَ ثُمَّ يَتَصَدَّقُ بِه
ترجمہ قدوری رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے کہا ہے کہ اگر وہ لقطہ دس درہم سے کم کا ہو تو چند دنوں تک اس کی شناخت اور تشہیر کراتا رہے اور اگر وہ دس درہم یا اس سے زیادہ کا ہو تو ایک سال تک اس کی شناخت کرا دے۔ مصنف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے کہا ہے کہ ابوحنیفہ رحمتہ اللہ علیہ سے یہ ایک روایت ہے ( اور ظاہر الروایہ میں دس درہم سے کم کا ہو یا زیادہ کا ہر حال میں ایک سال تک شناخت اور اعلان کراتا رہے۔) کم اس جگہ یہ بات جو کہی ہے کہ چند دن اس کی شناخت کرا دے تو اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ امام کی رائے پر عمل کیا جائے کہ جتنا وہ کہے اتنے دن شناخت کراتا رہے۔ اور امام محمد رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے مبسوط میں ایک سال کی تعیین کی ہے۔ اور اس میں کم قیمت یا زیادہ قیمت کے بارے میں کوئی تفصیل بیان نہیں کی ہے۔ امام مالک و شافعی رحمہما اللہ کا بھی یہی قول ہے۔ کیونکہ رسول اللہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ جو شخص لقطہ اٹھائے وہ
Translation: How many days should the announcement be made? He said: If it is less than ten dirhams, he announces it for some days; if it is ten or more, he announces it for a year. The weak servant (author) said: This is a narration from Abu Hanifa. His words 'days' mean according to what the Imam (ruler) sees. Muhammad in al-Asl estimated it as a year without distinction between little and much, and this is the saying of Malik and Shafi'i, due to his (peace be upon him) saying: 'Whoever picks up something, let him announce it for a year.' The face of the first view is that the estimation of a year came concerning a luqatah that was 100 dinars equal to 1000 dirhams, and ten and above are in the meaning of the thousand regarding the application of cutting (for theft) and regarding the permissibility of intercourse (for mahr), but they are not in its meaning regarding zakat. So we required announcement for a year out of precaution. What is below ten is not in the meaning of the thousand in any way, so we delegate to the opinion of the person afflicted (the finder). It was said: the correct view is that none of these amounts is binding, and it is delegated to the finder's opinion; he announces until it becomes clear that its owner will not seek it after that, then he gives it in charity.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling on the duration of ta'rif (announcement/identifying) of found property. According to Quduri's matn, if the item is worth less than 10 dirhams, the finder announces it for a few days; if 10 dirhams or more, for a full year. However, the commentary notes that this is one riwayah (narration) from Abu Hanifa. In the Zahir al-Riwayah (the relied-upon books of the madhhab), Muhammad's view is that the announcement should be for one year regardless of value, and this is supported by the hadith commanding announcement for a year. The justification for the distinction is that the amount of 10 dirhams is analogous to 1000 dirhams in matters of theft (where nisab is 10 dirhams) and mahr (where 10 dirhams is the minimum for sexual relations to be permissible), but not in zakat. So for caution, one year is required for 10 dirhams and above. For items below 10 dirhams, since no analogy to significant rulings exists, the duration is left to the discretion of the imam or the finder. The passage also mentions an alternative correct view that no fixed limit is binding, and the finder should announce until he is sure the owner has given up, then give it in charity.

Key Terms
التعريف (al-ta'rif): The act of publicly announcing or identifying found property to attempt to locate its owner
اللقطة (al-luqatah): Found property (including animals) that is taken by someone
درهم (dirham): Silver coin; standard measure of value in fiqh. 10 dirhams is a threshold for many rulings (nisab of theft, minimum mahr, etc.)
حول (hawl): A full lunar year (approximately 354 days)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi view (Zahir al-Riwayah), for how long must a finder announce found property worth 5 dirhams?
A) A few days.
B) One year.
C) Until the owner appears.
D) No announcement is needed.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position requires one year of announcement for all found property, based on the prophetic command.

The Finder's Liability in Luqata: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on finder's liability with proof and rebuttal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the finder's liability (damān) and explain the proof-text and rebuttal against Abu Yusuf's view.

Core Idea
Taking another's property creates strict liability; a good intention does not negate a certain obligation.

When you find lost property, are you automatically responsible for it if it gets damaged? The Hanafi school addresses this with a nuanced rule that balances the finder's good deed with legal accountability. This lesson unpacks the disagreement within the school, contrasting the majority view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad with the dissenting opinion of Abu Yusuf, who trusted the finder's good intent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Source
Begin by locating the statement that the finder is liable (ḍāmin) and note that this is attributed to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Then find Abu Yusuf's opposing view.
2
Analyze Abu Yusuf's Proof
Read why Abu Yusuf believes the finder is not liable: he relies on the apparent circumstance (ẓāhir al-ḥāl) that the finder did a good deed, so his word should be accepted.
3
Examine the Majority's Response
Understand the Hanafi response: the finder's confession of taking another's property establishes liability. His claim of good intention introduces doubt, but doubt cannot remove a certainty already fixed. Moreover, people act for self-interest, so ẓāhir al-ḥāl is ambiguous.
4
Evaluate the Practical Difference (Thamarah al-Khilaf)
Consider the consequence: under the majority view, if the finder claims the item was lost through no fault of his own, he remains liable. Under Abu Yusuf's view, he would not be liable if believed.
5
Confirm the Muftā Bihi Position
Note that the relied-upon position for fatwa is that the finder is liable (ḍāmin), following Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب اللقطة
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد پخته ملتقط ضامن ہوگا ۔ مگر امام ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے کہا ہے کہ وہ ضامن نہیں ہوگا۔ اور اٹھانے والے کی ہی بات قبول کی جائے گی کیونکہ ظاہر حال اسی کے لئے گواہ ہے کیونکہ اس نے تو ایک نیک کام کیا تھا، برا کام نہیں کیا تھا ۔ امام مالک و شافعی اور احمد رحمہم اللہ کا بھی یہی قول ہے۔) امام ابو حنیفہ امام محمد رحمہما اللہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس ملتقط نے خود ضمان لازم آنے کے سب یعنی غیرکا مال لینے کا اقرار کیا ساتھ ہی ایسی بات کا بھی دعوی کیا جس سے وہ اس ضمان سے بری ہو جائے یعنی یہ کہ میں نے یہ مال اس کے مالک کو دینے کے لئے لیا تھا)۔ اور ان دونوں باتوں کی وجہ سے اصل بات میں شک پیدا ہو گیا اس لئے اس کے اقرار کر لینے سے جو ضمان اس پر یقینی لازم ہو چکا تھا وہ اس شک کی وجہ سے ختم نہ ہوگا اور امام ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے جو ظا ہر حال کا ذکر کیا تو ویسی ہی ظاہر حالت اس کے مخالف بھی موجود ہے یعنی بظاہر ہر شخص جو کام بھی کرتا ہے وہ اپنی ہی ذات کے لئے کرتا ہے۔ واضح ہو کہ گواہ بنانے کے لئے اس ملتقط کا دوسرے سے اتنا کہ دینا کافی ہے کہ اگر تم لوگ کسی سے یا کہیں سے یہ سن کہ وہ اپنی کسی گمشدہ چیز کے لئے اعلان کر رہا ہو تو تم اسے میرا نام اور پتہ بتا دو یعنی اس چیز کی تعین ضروری نہیں ہے۔ اور یہ بات بھی معلوم ہونی چاہئے کہ یہ حکم عام ہے کہ خواہ لقطہ ایک ہو یا ایک سے زیادہ ہو کیونکہ لقطہ اسم جنس ہے۔ لیکن ملتقط کو چاہئے کہ اس چیز کی شناخت کر دے)
The Book of Luqata. Ashraf al-Hidaya, Urdu commentary of Hidaya, volume seven. The finder will be liable. However, Imam Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, said that he will not be liable. And the word of the finder will be accepted because the apparent circumstance bears witness for him, since he did a good deed, not a bad one. Imam Malik, al-Shafi'i, and Ahmad, may Allah have mercy on them, also hold this view. The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on them, is that this finder confessed to causing liability, i.e., taking another's property, and simultaneously claimed something that would absolve him from that liability, i.e., that he took this property to give to its owner. Due to both statements, doubt arose about the matter, so the liability that had become certain upon him due to his confession will not be removed by the doubt. As for Imam Abu Yusuf's mention of the apparent circumstance, there is also an apparent circumstance opposed to it, i.e., apparently every person does every action for his own self. It is clear that for making witnesses, it is sufficient for the finder to tell another: 'If you hear from someone or somewhere that someone is announcing for a lost item, then tell him my name and address,' i.e., identifying the item is not necessary. And it should also be known that this ruling is general, whether the found item is one or more, because luqata is a generic noun. But the finder should identify the item.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage addresses the liability of the finder of lost property (luqata). The default Hanafi position, held by Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, is that the finder becomes liable (ḍāmin) for the property when he picks it up. This is because by taking possession of someone else's property, he assumes a legal responsibility. Imam Abu Yusuf, however, held that the finder is not liable, and his word is accepted if he claims he took it with the intention of returning it to the owner. Abu Yusuf's reasoning is based on the apparent circumstance (ẓāhir al-ḥāl): the finder performed a commendable act, so he should be trusted. Imam Malik, al-Shafi'i, and Ahmad ibn Hanbal concur with Abu Yusuf. The passage explains the Hanafi proof: the finder's confession of taking the property establishes liability; his claim of intention to return it introduces doubt, but doubt does not remove a certainty (liability already established). Furthermore, the finder's self-interest undermines the presumption of altruism—people generally act for their own benefit. The passage also clarifies that for witnessing, the finder need not specify the exact item; he can merely ask others to direct any claimant to him. This ruling applies universally to any number of found items, as luqata is a generic term. However, the finder must still be able to identify the item when the owner appears.

Key Terms
ملتقط (multaqit): The finder of lost property (luqata).
ضامن (ḍāmin): Liable; one who must compensate for loss or damage.
لقطة (luqata): Lost property that is found and picked up by someone.
ظاہر حال (ẓāhir al-ḥāl): Legal presumption based on what appears to be the case; apparent circumstance.
اقرار (iqrār): Confession; a legally binding admission of fact.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main difference between the majority Hanafi view (Abu Hanifa & Muhammad) and Abu Yusuf's view regarding the finder's liability?
A) The majority say the finder is not liable; Abu Yusuf says he is liable.
B) The majority say the finder is liable; Abu Yusuf says he is not liable.
C) The majority require announcing for a year; Abu Yusuf does not.
D) They agree but differ on the length of announcement.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the finder of lost property is liable for it from the moment of taking possession, even if he intended to return it, because certainty from confession is not removed by doubt.

Luqatah — Found Property
