Explanation of the case: If the lost property is found with a poor person by way of charity, the original owner has the right to claim compensation in case it is lost, because the poor person took possession of it without the permission of the original owner. If it is still present, he is also entitled to take it back, because it is the original property of the owner. It should be known that in the aforementioned case under discussion, two matters are stated: 1. Discussion of compensation from the poor person for the charity. 2. Discussion of the specific property. And with Allah is success. Detailed discussion of both matters is available: 1. Discussion of compensation from the poor person for the charity: The finder, after the completion of the period, gave it in charity, and it was lost with the poor person. In this case, the owner is entitled to take compensation from the poor person, because the poor person took possession of the lost property without the permission of the owner, even though this possession came through the finder by way of charity. Since the finder does not have ownership rights over the lost property, therefore after charity, the poor person's ownership rights are also not established. This is why after finding the lost property, the finder is obligated to search for the owner by announcing it for one year or until the judge, the ruler, or the finder himself deems appropriate. When the finder's dominant thought is that the owner will not be found, then it is legally permissible to give the lost property in charity. But despite the charity, the owner still has the right to take his property as compensation from the poor person in case it is lost. And Allah knows best the correct. 2. Discussion of specific property: It should be known that the term 'ayn mal applies to property that is in reality the original and does not have a substitute in case of loss or destruction, because a substitute is not considered the original, regardless of how similar it may be to the original. For example, if a gold or silver item (like a ring) is lost after charity with the poor person, and when returning compensation to the owner, an item of similar gold or silver is given instead, that will not be considered the specific property, even though the compensation is fulfilled. If after charity the original property is still with the poor person, then when returning it as compensation, it will be the specific property. And the hadith of the Messenger (peace be upon him) says: 'Whoever finds his specific property, he has more right to it.' In this hadith, the greater right to the specific property is definitively established for the owner's ownership, but with the condition that the owner provides witnesses or complete identification marks to prove his specific property, because witnessing is based on strong evidence and identification marks serve as substitute for witnesses. Thus, with the presence of these (witnesses or complete marks), finding the specific property is confirmed. And Allah knows best the correct.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the situation where a finder of lost property gives it in charity to a poor person after the prescribed period of announcement. The author explains that the original owner has two rights: if the specific item still exists, he can reclaim it directly from the poor person because it is his 'ayn (specific property); if it is lost, he can demand compensation from the poor person. The reason is that the poor person took possession without the owner's permission—even though the finder gave it in charity, the finder himself does not own it, so he cannot transfer ownership. The commentary then defines 'ayn mal as property that is identical and not a substitute. The hadith "Man wajada 'ayna malihi fahuwa ahaqqu bih" is cited as proof, establishing the owner's superior right. The condition for reclaiming is that the owner must prove ownership through witnesses or clear marks.

Key Terms
عین مال ('ayn mal): Specific, identifiable property of the owner that is not a substitute or replacement.
تاوان (tawan): Compensation paid when the lost property is destroyed or lost after being taken without authorization.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Because the poor person must always guarantee the item.

Key Takeaway
The owner of lost property retains the right to reclaim the specific item or claim compensation even after it is given in charity, because the finder cannot transfer ownership.

Luqatah — Found Property

Ruling on Picking Up Large Animals as Lost Property
Dispute between Hanafis and Malikis/Shafi'is on picking up large animals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on picking up stray camels and cows as lost property and evaluate the Maliki/Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Taking a stray camel is mustahabb to protect property, even though it can defend itself.

This lesson explores a well-known inter-madhhab dispute about picking up large animals like camels and cows found in the desert. While the Hanafi school considers it recommended (mustahabb) to take and announce them, Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i hold that leaving them is better. We will examine the key arguments and the reasoning behind each position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school rules: it is permissible (ja'iz) and recommended (mustahabb) to pick up sheep, cows, and camels as lost property.
The matn says 'يَجُوزُ' (it is permissible), and the commentary clarifies it is mustahabb.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i say that for camels and cows in the desert, leaving them is better (afdal) than taking them.
Imam Ahmad also holds this view.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Their basis: the original ruling on taking another's property is haram; permissibility is only due to fear of loss (siya'). Since these animals can defend themselves, the loss risk is minimal, so taking is makruh and leaving is preferable.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: fear of loss still exists (e.g., from thieves or other dangers), so these animals remain luqatah where taking is mustahabb to preserve property, similar to sheep.
The commentary cites the hadith of Zayd ibn Khalid but explains it applies only when there is no fear of loss.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: a Hanafi would take and announce the animal, while a Maliki/Shafi'i would leave it, considering taking makruh.
This affects how a finder should act in such situations.

بفخر
بکریں ، گائے ، اونٹ کے لقطہ کا حکم
قَالَ وَيَجُوزُ الْالْتِقَاطُ فِى الشَّاةِ وَالْبَقَرِ وَالْبَعِيرِ وَقَالَ مَالِكِ وَالشَّافِعِي إِذَا وَجَدَ الْبَعِيرِ وَالْبَقَرِ فِي الصَّحْرَاءِ فَالشَّرْكُ أَفْضَلُ وَعَلى هَذَا الخِلافِ الْفَرَسِ لَهُمَا أنَّ الاِصْلَ فِى أحْدِ مَالِ الْغَيْرِ اخْرُمَةُ وَالْإِبَاحَةُ مَخَافَةَ الصِّيَاعِ وَإِذَا كَانَ مَعَهَا مَا يَدْفَعُ عَنْ نَّفْسِهَا يُقِلُّ الصِّيَاعُ وَلَكِنَّهُ يُتوهَمُ فَيُقْضَى بِالْكَرَاهَةِ وَالتَّدْبِ إِلَى التَّرْكِ وَلَتَا أَنَّهَا لُقْطَةٌ يَتَوَهَّمُ ضِيَا عُهَا فَيُسْتَحَبُّ أَخُذْهَا وَتَعْرِيفُهَا صِيَانَةُ لِأَمْوَالِ النَّاسِ كَمَا فِي الشَّاةِ
ترجمہ اور لقطہ کے طور پر بکری وگائے اور اونٹ کو بھی پکڑ کر رکھ لینا جائز ہے ۔ مگر امام مالک اور شافعی رحمہما اللہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ اگر اونٹ وگائے کو جنگل میں کوئی پائے تو اسے چھوڑ دینا افضل ہے۔ ( امام احمد حمتہ اللہ علیہ کا بھی یہی قول ہے)۔ اور یہ اختلاف گھوڑی کے بارے میں بھی ہے۔ امام مالک و شافعی رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ غیر کا مال لینے میں اصل حکم اس کا حرام ہونا ہے۔ البتہ اس کے مال کے ضائع ہونے کو پالینے کے خیال سے لے لینا بھی جائز ہے۔ اس لئے جب لقطہ ایسا مال یا جانور ہے جو خود کو غیر سے محفوظ کر سکتا ہو (جیسے گائے اور اونٹ میں ہے) تو اس کے ضائع ہونے کا خطرہ کم ہو جاتا ہے۔ اگر چہ اس کا امکان اور اس کا، ہم بھی باقی رہتا ہے۔ تو یہ حکم دیا جائے گا کہ اس کا پکڑ نافی الحال مکروہ ہے۔ اور نہ پکڑنا اچھا ہے۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اونٹ اور گائے بھی ایک لقطہ ہی ہے جس کے ضائع ہونے کا خوف پورا رہتا ہے۔ اس لئے اسے پکڑ کر اعلان کرادینا مستحب ہوگا۔ تاکہ لوگوں کے جانور محفوظ رہ سکیں ۔ جیسا کہ بکری کے
بارے میں حکم ہے۔
تشریح قال ويجوز الخ جانوروں کے لقطہ ہونے کی صورت میں گائے اور اونٹ جیسے بڑے جانور چونکہ اپنی حفاظت خود کر سکتے ہیں۔ اس لئے اسے پکڑ کر حفاظت کرنے کی خاص ضرورت نہیں رہتی ہے۔ البتہ اگر بکری ہو تو اس کے ضائع ہونے کا خطرہ زیادہ ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے بطور لقطہ اسے پکڑ کر اس کی حفاظت قاضی کی اجازت کے ساتھ کرنی چاہئے ۔ حضرت زید بن خالد کی حدیث میں ہے کہ ایک شخص نے رسول اللہ سے لفظہ کے بارے میں دریافت کیا۔ تو فرمایا کہ ایک سال تک اس کا اعلان کیا جائے ۔ انہوں نے پھر پوچھا کہ بھٹکی ہوئی بکری کا کیا حکم ہے۔ تو فرمایا کہ تم اسے پکڑ لو کہ وہ تمہارے کسی بھائی کی ہے یعنی اصل مالک کی ہے یا تمہاری ہے یا بھیڑیے کی تو ہے۔ انہوں نے پھر پوچھا کہ یا رسول اللہ پھر بھٹکے ہوئے اونٹ کا کیا حکم ہے۔ تو رسول اللہ نغصہ ہو گئے ۔ یہاں تک کہ آپ کے رخسار مبارک سرخ ہو گئے اور فرمایا کہ تم کو اس سے کیا تعلق ہے۔ کہ اس کے ساتھ ہی اس کے کھانے اور پینے کا انتظام موجود ہے۔ یہاں تک کہ اس کا مالک خود اسے یا لے۔ (رواہ البخاری) اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ یہ حکم آپ نے ایسی صورت میں فرمایا ہے کہ اونٹ کے ضائع ہونے کا خوف نہ تھا۔ اس لئے اگر کسی وقت اس کے بارے میں خوف ہو تو اسے پکڑ لینا ہی اولی ہوگا۔
Book of Lost Property. Ashraf al-Hidaya commentary on Hidaya, volume. Ruling on picking up sheep, cows, and camels. He said: It is permissible to pick up sheep, cows, and camels. Malik and Shafi'i said: If one finds a camel or cow in the desert, leaving it is better. And the same difference applies to a mare. Their argument is that the original ruling on taking another's property is prohibition; permissibility is only due to fear of loss. And when the animal can defend itself, the chance of loss is reduced. But even though it may be imagined, it is ruled as makruh, and leaving is better. Our argument is that it is a lost item whose loss is feared, so taking it and announcing it is mustahabb in order to protect people's property, just as with sheep. Translation: It is permissible to pick up sheep, cows, and camels as lost property. However, Imam Malik and Shafi'i said that if one finds a camel or cow in the desert, leaving it is better (Imam Ahmad also holds this view). And this difference applies to the mare. The proof of Imam Malik and Shafi'i is that the original ruling on taking another's property is prohibition; however, taking it is permissible due to the fear of loss. So when the lost item is an animal that can defend itself (like a cow or camel), the risk of loss is reduced. Though the possibility remains, the ruling is that taking it is makruh, and leaving it is good. Our proof is that the camel and cow are also lost items whose loss is still feared, so taking them and announcing is mustahabb to protect people's property, just as with sheep. Explanation: He said 'it is permissible' etc. In the case of large animals like cows and camels, since they can protect themselves, there is no specific need to pick them up for protection. However, if it is a sheep, the risk of loss is greater, so one should pick it up as lost property and protect it with the permission of the judge. In the hadith of Zayd ibn Khalid, a man asked the Prophet about lost property. He said: Announce it for a year. He then asked about a stray sheep. He said: Take it, for it is either for your brother (the owner), or for you, or for the wolf. He then asked about a stray camel. The Prophet became angry until his cheeks reddened and said: What have you to do with it? It has its own provisions and water until its owner finds it. (Bukhari) The response is that this ruling was given in a situation where there was no fear of loss for the camel. Therefore, if there is fear at any time, taking it is preferable.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding picking up larger animals (camels, cows) as lost property. The Hanafi position (from the matn) is that it is permissible (ja'iz) to pick up sheep, cows, and camels. Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i argue that for camels and cows in the desert, leaving them is afdal (better) because they can defend themselves, so the excuse of preservation is weaker. The Hanafi response, as given in the commentary, is that these animals are still considered luqatah and there is still a fear of loss (especially from predators or thieves), so taking them and announcing is mustahabb (recommended) to protect people's property, just as with sheep. The commentary also cites the hadith of Zayd ibn Khalid where the Prophet became angry about the camel question, but explains that this was because at that time there was no fear of loss; in times of fear, taking it is better.

Key Terms
التقاط (iltiqat): The act of picking up and taking possession of lost property with the intention of preserving it.
لقطة (luqatah): Lost property that is found and taken; the subject of specific rulings.
صیاع (siya'): Loss or waste; the danger of the property being lost or destroyed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on picking up a stray camel in the desert?
A) Forbidden (haram).
B) Makruh (disliked) and leaving is better.
C) Mustahabb (recommended) to take and announce.
D) Obligatory (fard).

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends taking and announcing stray large animals as lost property to protect people's assets, even if they can fend for themselves.

Expenses on Lost Property Without Judge's Permission
Ruling on finder's expenses: without permission = voluntary, with permission = reimbursable

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on expenses incurred by the finder of lost property without the judge's permission and distinguish it from the scenario with permission.

Core Idea
Without the judge's permission, the finder is a volunteer — no reimbursement.

This lesson addresses a specific issue in the law of luqatah: what happens when the finder (multaqit) spends money on the lost property? The Hanafi school distinguishes between spending with and without judicial authorization. The core principle is that the judge has wilaya over the property of the absent owner, so his permission makes the expenditure reimbursable; without it, the finder is considered a mutabarri' (volunteer). Let's examine the textual basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
State the two cases: spending without the judge's permission and spending with the judge's permission.
The passage clearly contrasts these two scenarios.
2
Determine the legal consequence for each
For without permission: the finder is a mutabarri' (volunteer) and cannot claim reimbursement. For with permission: the expense is upon the owner, who must reimburse.
The term 'mutabarri' is key.
3
Understand the underlying rationale
The judge has wilayah (authority) over the property of the absent owner, so his permission makes the expenditure binding. Without it, the finder's authority is deficient.
The phrase 'لقصور ولايته عن ذمة المالك' explains the deficiency.
4
Note the mufta bihi
This is the standard Hanafi position from Zahir al-Riwayah.
The ruling is consistent across the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ملتقط نے بغیر اجازت حاکم کے لقطہ پر خرچ کیا تو تبرع شمار ہوگا
فَإِنْ أنْفَقَ الْمُلْتَقِطْ عَلَيْهَا بِغَيْرِ إِذْنِ الْحَاكِمِ فَهُوَ مَتَبَرْعُ لِقُصُورٍ وِلَا يَتِهِ عَنْ ذِمَّةِ الْمَالِكِ وَإِنْ أَنْفَقَ بِأَمْرِهِ كَانَ ذَالِكَ عَلَى صَاحِبِهَا لِأَنَّ الْقَاضِي وِلَا يَةٌ فِى مَالِ الْغَائِبِ نَظَرَالَهُ وَقَدْ يَكُونُ النَّظَرُ فِي الْإِنْفَاقِ عَلَى مَانُبَيِّنُ
If the finder spends on it without the permission of the judge, then he is a volunteer (mutabarri') due to the deficiency of his authority over the owner's liability. And if he spends by his (the judge's) command, then that is upon the owner, because the judge has authority over the property of the absent person as a consideration for him. And consideration may be in spending, as we will explain.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage states a ruling on expenses incurred by the finder (multaqit) on the lost property. Two scenarios: (1) Without the judge's permission: the finder is considered a volunteer (mutabarri'), meaning he cannot claim reimbursement from the owner because his authority is incomplete. (2) With the judge's permission: the judge has wilaya (authority) over the property of the absent owner, so the expense is valid and the owner must reimburse. This is based on the principle that the judge acts in the interest of the absent owner.

Key Terms
متبّرع (mutabarri'): One who does an act voluntarily without expectation of compensation or reimbursement.
ولایت (wilayah): Legal authority or guardianship, here specifically the judge's authority over the property of an absent person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a finder spends money on maintaining a lost animal without getting permission from the judge, what is the ruling?
A) The owner must reimburse the finder.
B) The finder is considered a volunteer and cannot claim reimbursement.
C) The finder can claim reimbursement if the expense was necessary.
D) The finder becomes the owner of the animal.

Key Takeaway
The finder's expenses on lost property are only reimbursable with the judge's permission; without it, the finder is a volunteer.

Picking Up Lost Animals: The Hanafi View and Disagreement with Malik and Shafi'i
States permissibility and disagreement with Malik and Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on picking up lost camels and cows in the desert and explain the disagreement with Malik and Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Preserving potential loss justifies picking up even large animals; fear of loss outweighs original prohibition.

When you find a lost camel or cow in the desert, should you pick it up or leave it? The Hanafi school says it is recommended to pick it up and announce it, just like a lost sheep. But Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i held that for large animals that can defend themselves, it is better to leave them. Let us examine the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the two positions
The dispute is about picking up large lost animals (camel, cow, horse) in the desert. Hanafi: permissible/recommended; Malik/Shafi'i: leaving is better.
2
Understand the opposing proof
Malik and Shafi'i argue that the default ruling on taking others' property is prohibition; the exception is allowed only when there is real fear of loss. Large animals can defend themselves, reducing that fear.
They view the risk of loss as minimal.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi school argues that these animals are still luqatah whose loss is feared. Therefore, picking them up is mustahabb to preserve property, analogous to sheep.
The analogy (qiyas) to sheep is key.
4
Recognize the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis will pick up and announce; others may leave them without responsibility.
5
Note the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is relied upon due to the stronger evidence of preserving property.
Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah supports this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَيَجُوزُ الْالْتِقَاطُ فِى الشَّاةِ وَالْبَقَرِ وَالْبَعِيرِ وَقَالَ مَالِكِ وَالشَّافِعِي إِذَا وَجَدَ الْبَعِيرِ وَالْبَقَرِ فِي الصَّحْرَاءِ فَالشَّرْكُ أَفْضَلُ وَعَلى هَذَا الخِلافِ الْفَرَسِ لَهُمَا أنَّ الاِصْلَ فِى أَخْذِ مَالِ الْغَيْرِ حُرْمَةٌ وَالْإِبَاحَةُ مَخَافَةَ الصِّيَاعِ وَإِذَا كَانَ مَعَهَا مَا يَدْفَعُ عَنْ نَّفْسِهَا يُقِلُّ الصِّيَاعُ وَلَكِنَّهُ يُتوهَمُ فَيُقْضَى بِالْكَرَاهَةِ وَالتَّرْكُ أَوْلَى وَلَنَا أَنَّهَا لُقْطَةٌ يَتَوَهَّمُ ضِيَاعُهَا فَيُسْتَحَبُّ أَخْذُهَا وَتَعْرِيفُهَا صِيَانَةُ لِأَمْوَالِ النَّاسِ كَمَا فِي الشَّاةِ
He said: Picking up sheep, cows, and camels is permissible. Malik and al-Shafi'i said: If one finds a camel or cow in the desert, leaving it is better. And the horse follows the same disagreement. Their proof: The original rule regarding taking the property of another is prohibition; permissibility is due to fear of loss. When it has what defends itself, the risk of loss is reduced, but it is still feared, so it is ruled makruh and leaving is better. Our proof: It is a found item whose loss is feared, so picking it up and announcing it is recommended as a preservation of people's property, just as with the sheep.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute. The Hanafi school (Imam Abu Hanifa and his companions) holds that picking up lost sheep, cows, and camels is permissible and recommended (mustahabb). Malik and al-Shafi'i argue that for large animals like camels and cows that can defend themselves in the desert, it is better to leave them because the original ruling on taking others' property is prohibition, and the exception of fear of loss is reduced. The Hanafi response: even though they can defend themselves, the possibility of loss still exists, so they are like sheep — picking them up and announcing them is recommended to preserve people's property. The same ruling applies to horses.

Key Terms
لُقْطَة (luqatah): A lost item (animal) found by someone.
مَالِك (Malik): Imam Malik ibn Anas, founder of the Maliki school.
شَافِعِيّ (al-Shafi'i): Imam Muhammad ibn Idris al-Shafi'i, founder of the Shafi'i school.
صِيَاع (siya'): Loss, waste, or getting lost.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, picking up a lost camel in the desert is:
A) Haram
B) Makruh
C) Mustahabb (recommended)
D) Wajib

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends picking up all lost animals, including large ones like camels, to preserve property, despite their ability to defend themselves.

Judge's Options for a Found Animal
Explains judge's options: hire, sell, or spend

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to STATE the three options available to a judge for a found animal and EXPLAIN the rationale (talil) for each based on maslahah.

Core Idea
The judge preserves the owner's wealth by choosing the most beneficial option for a found animal.

When a found animal is brought to the judge, he must decide how to handle it in a way that protects the owner's property. The judge has several discretionary options based on the animal's characteristics and the likely costs. This passage from Al-Hidayah explains each option and the legal reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
Read the passage and list the three situations the judge considers: (1) the animal has a benefit, (2) the animal has no benefit and costs exceed value, (3) spending is more beneficial and owner may appear.
These scenarios cover most found animals.
2
Determine the judge's action for each
For each scenario, note what the judge does: hires out, sells, or permits spending with debt. Understand the link between the scenario and the action.
The action is based on what best preserves the asset.
3
Analyze the rationale (talil)
For each action, the passage gives a reason. For hiring: preserves the animal without imposing debt. For selling: preserves value when physical preservation is impossible. For spending: allows temporary care hoping owner appears.
The reason (illah) is rooted in maslahah.
4
Note the temporal limit on spending
The passage adds that spending is only permitted for two or three days, pending the owner's appearance. This balances care with avoiding indefinite debt.
This shows the judge's discretion is bounded.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا رُفِعَ ذَالِكَ إِلَى الْحَاكِمِ نَظَرَ فِيهِ فَإِنْ كَانَ لِلْبَهِيمَةِ مَنْفَعَةُ اجَرَهَا وَأَنْفَقَ عَلَيْهَا مِنْ أَجْرَتِهَا لِأَنَّ فِيْهِ إِبْقَاءُ الْعَيْنِ عَلى مَلْكِهِ مِنْ غَيرِ الزَامِ الدِّينِ عَلَيْهِ وَكَذَالِكَ يَفْعَلُ بِالْعَبْدِ الْآبِقِ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهَا مَنْفَعَةٌ وَخَافَ أنْ تَسْتَغْرِقَ التَّفَقَةُ قِيَمَتَهَا بَاعَهَا وَأَمَرَ بِحِفْظِ تَمَنِهَا إِبْقَاء لَهُ مَعْنَى عِندَ تَعَدُّرِ بقَائِهِ صُورَةً وَإِنْ كَانَ الأصَلَحُ الإنْفَاقِ عَلَيْهَا أَذِنَ فِي ذَالِكَ وَجَعَلَ التَّفَقَةَ دَيْنًا عَلَى مَالِكِهَا لِأَنَّهُ نُصِبَ نَاظِرًا وَفِي هَذَا نَظَرُ مِنَ الْجَانِبَيْنِ قَالُوا إِنَّمَا يَأْمُرُ بِالإِ نُفَاقِ يَوْمَيْنِ أَوْ تَلَثَةَ أَيَّامٍ عَلَى قَدْرِ مَايَرَى رَجَاءٌ أَنْ يَظْهَرَ مَالِكُهَا فَإِذَالَمْ يَظْهَرُ
And when that is brought to the judge, he looks into it. If the animal has a benefit, he hires it out and spends on it from its hire, because in that is preservation of the asset in his ownership without imposing a debt on him. Similarly, he does with a runaway slave. And if it has no benefit and he fears that the expenditure will consume its value, he sells it and orders its price to be preserved, preserving its meaning [value] when its physical preservation is impossible. And if spending on it is more beneficial, he permits that and makes the expenditure a debt on its owner, because he is appointed as a custodian, and in this is consideration from both sides. They said: He only orders spending for two or three days according to what he sees, hoping that its owner may appear; and if he does not appear...
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage explains the judge's procedure when a found animal is brought to him. The judge has three options based on what is most beneficial (maslahah): 1) If the animal can generate income (e.g., milk, wool, or labor), the judge hires it out and uses the income for its upkeep. This preserves the animal without burdening the owner with debt. The same applies to a runaway slave. 2) If the animal has no income and the cost of feeding it would exhaust its value, the judge sells it and preserves the sale price. This preserves the owner's wealth in value even if the physical animal is lost. 3) If it is more beneficial to spend on the animal (e.g., if the owner may appear soon), the judge permits the finder to spend and makes that expenditure a debt on the owner. However, this permission is only for a short period (two or three days) pending the owner's appearance.

Key Terms
مَنْفَعَة (manfa'ah): Benefit or utility that can generate income (e.g., milk, wool, labor).
أَجَرَ (ajara): To hire out or lease for a fee.
تَمَن (thaman): Price or value; the proceeds from sale.
مَصْلَحَة (maslahah): Benefit or public interest, the basis for the judge's discretion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a found cow can produce milk, the judge should:
A) Sell it immediately
B) Hire it out and spend from its income
C) Keep it without spending
D) Slaughter and distribute the meat

Key Takeaway
The judge must choose the action that best preserves the owner's wealth, whether through hiring, selling, or short‑term debt, based on the animal's benefit and costs.

Finder's Expenses: Voluntary vs. Qadi-Authorized
Ruling on finder's expenses without and with qadi's permission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two scenarios of finder's expenses in Hanafi law and state the legal consequences for each.

Core Idea
Without qadi permission, the finder's expense is charity; with permission, it's a debt.

This passage from the Sharh of Al-Hidayah draws a critical distinction between a finder's voluntary spending on a lost animal and spending authorized by the qadi. The legal effects differ fundamentally: one is an act of benevolence with no claim, the other creates a binding debt on the owner. Understanding this distinction is essential for anyone dealing with lost property (luqatah) to avoid unjust enrichment or liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its two scenarios
The act is the finder (multaqit) spending on the lost animal. There are two scenarios: without qadi permission and with qadi permission.
2
Determine the legal nature for each scenario
Without permission: it is ihsan (charity), not a binding debt. With permission: it becomes a dayn (debt) on the owner.
This is the core distinction.
3
Understand the underlying principle
The finder has limited authority; only the qadi can bind the absent owner's property because he has guardianship over the absent person's interests.
The qadi acts as nazir for the absent owner.
4
Apply the rule to a new case
If a finder buys a rope for the animal without qadi permission, can he claim the cost? No, same principle applies: it is charity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ہفتم ۱۸۵ ترجمه فان انفق الملتقط پھر اگر جانور کو پکڑ لینے والے ( ملتقط ) نے اس جانور کو قاضی کی اجازت اور حکم کے بغیر از خود دانہ اور چارہ دیا تو اسے احسان کرنے والا کہا جائے گا ۔ اور مالک پر اس کی ذمہ داری نہیں آئے گی کیونکہ اس ملتقط کی ذمہ داری محدود ہے رے پر یہ شخص کچھ بھی لازم نہیں کر سکتا ہے۔ البتہ اگر قاضی کے حکم سے جانور کو کھانا پینا دیا تو یہ خرچ جانور کے مالک پر قرض ہوتا جائے گا کیونکہ قاضی کو یہ حق حاصل ہوتا ہے کہ غائب شخص کے مال میں اس کی بہتری کے لئے انتظام کرے کبھی غائب شخص پر بھلائی کرتے ہوئے اس کے جانور کو نفقہ یعنی چارہ دانہ دینا ہوتا ہے۔ جیسا کہ اس مسئلہ کو ہم آئندہ پھر بیان کریں گے۔
Translation: For if the finder (multaqit) feeds the animal without the qadi's permission, he is called a charitable person. No liability falls on the owner because the finder's responsibility is limited, and this person cannot obligate anything. However, if he feeds it by the qadi's order, this expense becomes a debt on the owner because the qadi has the right to manage the absent person's property for his benefit, and sometimes it is for the absent person's good to feed his animal. As we will explain this issue later.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage clarifies the legal status of expenses incurred by a finder of a lost animal. The Sharh explains that if the finder spends out of his own initiative without authorization from the qadi, his action is considered ihsan (charitable benevolence). He acts voluntarily and cannot claim reimbursement from the owner. The reason is that the finder's duty is only to protect the property, not to obligate the owner without authorization. However, if the qadi orders the finder to feed the animal, then those expenses become a debt (dayn) upon the owner. This is because the qadi is the legal guardian (nazir) for the absent owner and has authority to bind the owner's property for necessary expenses. The passage ends by noting that this will be elaborated later. The key distinction is qadi's permission vs. lack thereof. This ruling is from the Hanafi school and is part of the chapter on luqatah (found property).

Key Terms
الملتقط (al-multaqit): The finder of a lost property (luqatah). In this context, specifically the person who finds and takes possession of a lost animal.
إحسان (ihsan): Benevolence, doing good. In this context, the finder's action of spending without qadi's permission is considered a charitable act.
قرض (qard): Debt. Here, the expense incurred by the finder with qadi's permission becomes a debt owed by the owner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person finds a lost goat and feeds it without the qadi's permission, can he later demand this expense from the owner?
A) Yes, because he preserved the goat.
B) Yes, if he can prove his expense.
C) No, it is considered charity; he cannot claim.
D) No, because the qadi must authorize first.

Key Takeaway
Expenses on a found animal without qadi authorization are charity; only qadi-authorized expenses create a binding debt on the owner.

Qadi's Management Options for Found Animals
Qadi's three options: hire, sell, or authorize expenses as debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three options a qadi has for managing a found animal and identify the condition that triggers each option.

Core Idea
A qadi must choose hire, sell, or expense-as-debt to preserve the owner's property—each option tied to the animal's benefit and expense risk.

This lesson examines the qadi's discretionary authority over a found animal (luqatah). The text from al-Hidayah presents a hierarchy of decisions based on whether the animal has beneficial use, whether expenses threaten to consume its value, and whether short-term maintenance is feasible. We will trace each option's rationale and the mashayikh's time limitation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
The passage outlines three situations: (1) the animal has benefit (manfa'ah), (2) it has no benefit and expenses exhaust its value, (3) spending on it is more beneficial. Identify each in the Arabic text.
2
Match each scenario to its ruling
For each scenario, determine the qadi's action: hire out and spend from hire, sell and preserve price, or authorize spending as debt.
3
Understand the underlying principle
The qadi's goal is to preserve the owner's property (ibqa' al-mal). Each option balances saving the 'ayn (physical item) or its value when the 'ayn cannot be preserved.
4
Note the time limitation
The mashayikh add that the qadi should only order spending for 2-3 days in hope of the owner's appearance; if no owner appears, sale is ordered because indefinite spending is destructive.
This is a practical restriction from later scholars.

When this is brought to the judge, he looks into it. If the animal has benefit, he hires it out and spends from its hire, because this preserves the item in its owner's ownership without obligating debt upon him. Similarly, he does with a runaway slave. Translation: ... [Urdu explanation]. And if it has no benefit and he fears that expenses will consume its value, he sells it and orders preservation of its price, preserving its meaning when its form cannot be preserved. Translation: ... [Urdu]. And if it is better to spend on it, he authorizes that and makes the expense a debt upon its owner, because he has been appointed as an administrator, and in this there is consideration from both sides. They said: He only orders spending for two or three days according to what he sees, hoping that its owner may appear. If he does not appear, he orders its sale, because the liability of spending is destructive, and there is no consideration in spending for a long period.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage details the authority and procedure of the qadi when a found animal (luqatah) is brought before him. The qadi must evaluate the situation and choose the option that best preserves the owner's property. Three scenarios are given: (1) If the animal can generate income (e.g., a milking goat, a riding animal, a runaway slave who can work), the qadi should hire it out and use the proceeds to cover its expenses. This way, the owner's property remains intact without incurring a debt. (2) If the animal has no productive benefit and the ongoing expenses would exhaust its entire value, the qadi should sell it and preserve the sale proceeds. Though the physical item is lost, its value is saved for the owner. (3) If it is more beneficial to keep and maintain the animal, the qadi may authorize the finder to spend on it, making those expenses a debt on the owner. However, the scholars (mashayikh) caution that the qadi should only order spending for a short period (two or three days) in the hope the owner appears. If the owner does not appear within that time, the qadi should order the sale, because indefinite spending would consume the animal's value. This ruling balances the interests of both the finder and the absent owner.

Key Terms
منفعة (manfa'ah): Benefit or utility that can generate income, such as milk, labor, or use.
أجرة (ujrah): Hire or rent income derived from the animal's use.
تفقة (nafaqah): Expenses for feeding and maintaining the animal.
قيمة (qimah): Market value of the animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Immediately sell it
B) Hire it out and use milk income for expenses
C) Keep it without any action
D) Give it to the finder

Key Takeaway
A qadi must match his action to the found animal's condition: hire if benefit, sell if expenses destroy value, or spend as debt briefly if hopeful.

The Requirement of Bayyinah Before Qadi Orders Spending
Imam Muhammad's requirement of bayyinah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the requirement of bayyinah for a luqatah finder and explain the rationale.

Core Idea
Evidence (bayyinah) is required to distinguish a trustee (amin) from a usurper (ghasib).

When a person claims to have found a lost animal and seeks the qadi's permission to spend on it, the qadi must ensure the finder is not a usurper. Imam Muhammad, in al-Asl, stipulated that the finder must produce evidence (bayyinah) to prove he is a trustee. This lesson examines the rationale for this requirement and the practical consequences of failing to produce evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
Imam Muhammad stipulates establishing evidence (bayyinah) before the qadi orders spending on a found animal. The basis is the possibility (ihtimal) that the finder may be a usurper (ghasib).
The qadi only orders spending for a trust (amanah), not for a usurpation.
2
Understand the nature of the evidence
The evidence is not for the purpose of a judicial ruling (qada') but to disclose the true situation (kashf al-hal). The qadi needs to know whether the finder is an amin or a ghasib.
If the finder claims no evidence, the qadi tells him to spend at his own risk.
3
Analyze the consequence
If the finder produces evidence and is truthful, he can claim reimbursement from the owner. If he lacks evidence and turns out to be a usurper, he cannot claim back the expenses.
The evidence protects both parties.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Muhammad's view is considered sahih (correct) in the school. Some early Hanafi scholars may not have required evidence, but the mufta bihi is to require it.
Al-Marghinani supports Imam Muhammad's position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَفِي الْأَصْلِ شَرَطَ إِقَامَةَ الْبَيِّنَةِ وَهُوَ الصَّحِيحُ لِأَنَّهُ يَحْتَمِلُ أَنْ يَكُونَ غَصْبًا فِي يَدِهِ وَلَا يَأْمُرُفِيهِ بِالْإِنْفَاقِ وَإِنَّمَا يَأْمُرُبِهِ فِي الْوَدِيْعَةِ فَلَا بُدَّ مِنَ الْبَيِّنَةِ لِكَشْفِ الْحَالِ وَلَيْسَتِ الْبَيِّنَةُ تُقَامُ لِلْقَضَاءِ وَإِنْ قَالَ لَاَيّنَةَ لِى يَقُوْلُ الْقَاضِي لَهُ أَنْفِقُ عَلَيْهِ إِنْ كُنتَ صَادِقَا فِيمَا قُلْتَ حَتَّى تَرْجِعَ عَلَى الْمَالِكِ إِنْ كَانَ صَادِقًا وَلَا يَرْجِعُ إِنْ كَانَ غَاصِبًا وَقَوْلُهُ فِي الْكِتَابِ وَجَعَلَ النَفَقَةَ دَيْنًا عَلَى صَاحِبِهَا إِشَارَةُ إِلَى أَنَّهُ إِنَّمَا يَرْجِعُ جانور کو نفقہ ( دانہ یا چارہ ) دیا جائے تو اس ملتقط کو اس بات کی اجازت دے دے اور اس کے خرچ کو اس کے مالک کے ذمہ قرض قرار دے دے ( یعنی بطور قرض اس پر خرچ کرتا رہے کیونکہ حاکم کو ہر ایک پر نظر رکھنے کا حکم ہے۔ اور مذکورہ انتظام ہی میں اصل مالک اور اس ملتقط پر بہتری کی نظر ہوگی۔ اس موقع میں مشائخ رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ حاکم ملتقط کو صرف دو یا تین دن جو مناسب سمجھے دانہ اور چارہ دینے کا حکم دے۔ اس امید پر کہ شاید ان دو تین دنوں میں مالک آ جائے ۔ اب اگر اس وقت تک مالک نہ آئے تو اس جانور کو فروخت کرنے کا اسے حکم دے دے کیونکہ اس طرح اسے چارہ مستقلاً یا بہت زیادہ دنوں تک کھلاتے رہنے سے جانور کی اصل قیمت سے اس وقت کا خرچ بہت زیادہ ہو جائے گا۔ اس طرح وہ جانور فروخت ہو کر ہاتھ سے بالکل نکل جائے گا۔ اور ایسا کرنے میں کوئی بھلائی نہیں ہوگی ۔ مصنف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ امام محمد رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے مبسوط میں شرط لگائی ہے کہ نفقہ کا حکم اس وقت دے گا جبکہ اس بات پر گواہ پیش کر دے۔ اور یہی قول صحیح ہے۔ کیونکہ یہاں یہ احتمال رہتا ہے کہ شاید اس شخص نے اس جانور پر غصب کے طور پر قبضہ کر رکھا ہو۔ حالانکہ ایسی صورت میں تو قاضی کبھی بھی اسے نفقہ دینے کا حکم نہیں دے گا۔ بلکہ صرف امانت کی صورت میں حکم دے سکتا ہے۔ اس لئے امانہ رکھنے پر گواہی کا ہونا ضروری ہوگا ۔ تاکہ حقیقت حال کچھ معلوم ہو۔ یہ گواہی اس لئے نہیں ہوگی کہ قاضی کا حکم ثابت ہو ( ۔ جس میں مدعا علیہ کوفکر کی ضرورت ہوتی ہے ) اور اگر ملتقط نے گواہ پیش کرنے سے انکار کر دیا تب قاضی اُسے یہ کہے گا کہ اگر تم اپنے قول میں بچے ہو ( جس کی حقیقت بعد میں ظاہر ہوگی ) تو اس کو دانہ چارہ دیا کرو۔ اگر دفعتہ وہ سچا ثابت ہو جائے تو مالک سے یہ خرچ واپس لے گا ۔ اور اگر اس کا غاصب ہونا ثابت ہو جائے تو خرچ واپس نہیں ملے گا ۔ اور کتاب میں جو یہ فرمایا ہے کہ قاضی یہ نفقہ اس کے مالک پر فرض ہونے کا حکم دے گا۔ تو اس کہنے میں اس بات کی طرف اشارہ ہے کہ اس جانور کے مالک کے آ جانے کے بعد اگر جانور فروخت نہیں کیا گیا اور قاضی پہلے ہی جانور کے نفقہ کو مالک پر قرض ہونے کے بارے میں کہہ چکا ہوتو یہ ملتقط اپنا پورا خرچ جانور کے مالک سے اسی صورت میں واپس لے سکتا ہے کہ قاضی نے قرض کے طور پر مالک سے واپس لینے کی شرط کر دی ہو اور یہی روایت اصح ہے ) ۔ اور اگر صرف خرچ کرنے کے لئے تو کہا مگر مالک پر اسے قرض ہونے کی شرط نہیں کی ہو تو اس سے واپس نہیں مانگ سکتا ہے)۔ تشریح ملحق شخص جانور کو قاضی کے سامنے پیش کرے گا قاضی دو تین دن تک جانور پر خرچ کرنے کا حکم دے گا کہ مالک کے آنے کا احتمال ہے اور یہ کم مدت مالک کے حق میں بہتر ہے اور زیادہ مدت میں بہتری کا پہلو نہیں اور ملتقط کا قیام شہادت ضروری ہے تا کہ غصب کا احتمال دور ہو جائے اور ملقط اس خرچ کو مالک سے لے لینے کا اختیار رکھتا ہے جبکہ قاضی نے نفقہ کیلئے قرض کی شرط لگائی ہے ۔
He said: In al-Asl, Imam Muhammad stipulated establishing evidence, and this is correct, because it is possible that it may be a usurpation in his hand, and he does not order spending on it; rather, he only orders spending in the case of a trust. So evidence is necessary to reveal the situation, and the evidence is not established for the sake of judicial ruling. And if he says 'I have no evidence,' the qadi says to him: 'Spend on it if you are truthful in what you say, so that you may claim reimbursement from the owner if you are truthful, and you cannot claim if you are a usurper.' And his statement in the book (al-Hidayah) 'and he made the expense a debt upon its owner' is an indication that he can only claim from the owner after he appears and the luqatah has not been sold, provided the qadi stipulated the claim upon the owner. And this is one narration, and it is the most correct. ... [Urdu translation and commentary] ... Explanation: The finder will bring the animal before the qadi. The qadi will order spending for two or three days, as there is hope of the owner's appearance; this short period is better for the owner, and there is no benefit in a longer period. The finder's establishment of evidence is necessary to remove the possibility of usurpation. The finder has the right to take the expense from the owner if the qadi stipulated the debt for the expense.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage addresses two important procedural issues from Imam Muhammad's al-Mabsut: the requirement of bayyinah (testimony) and the condition for reimbursement. First, when a person claims to be a finder of a lost animal and seeks qadi's authorization to spend on it, he must produce witnesses that he is indeed a trustee (amin) and not a usurper (ghasib). Imam Muhammad stipulates this as a precaution because the qadi's order to spend is only for amanah, not for a ghasib. The evidence is not for the purpose of a judicial ruling (qada') but to ascertain the truth. If the claimant cannot produce evidence, the qadi says, 'Spend if you are truthful; if you are truthful, you may claim from the owner; if you are a usurper, you cannot claim.' This encourages honesty. Second, the text clarifies that the finder can only claim reimbursement from the owner after the owner appears and the animal has not been sold, and only if the qadi explicitly stipulated that the expense is a debt repayable by the owner. This latter condition is essential; without it, the finder cannot demand repayment. The passage notes that this is the most correct narration (al-asahh) within the Hanafi school. This ruling protects both parties: the owner from unjustified claims, and the honest finder who acted under judicial authority.

Key Terms
بينة (bayyinah): Evidence or testimony; specifically, witnesses to prove that the finder found the animal as luqatah, not as a ghasp.
غصب (ghasb): Usurpation; wrongful possession of someone else's property. If the finder is a usurper, he is not entitled to any reimbursement.
صحيح (sahih): Correct; Imam Muhammad's view is considered the sahih (sound) position.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, what must a finder do before the qadi authorizes spending on a found animal with a guarantee of reimbursement?
A) Hand over the animal to the qadi.
B) Produce evidence (bayyinah) that he is a trustee.
C) Swear an oath.
D) Pay a deposit.

Key Takeaway
A luqatah finder must produce bayyinah to qualify for qadi-ordered spending with guarantee; otherwise, spending is at his own risk.

The Condition of Stipulation for Reimbursement
Condition for reimbursement: stipulation of debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the condition for a luqatah finder to claim reimbursement and distinguish between the two narrations.

Core Idea
Reimbursement is only guaranteed if the qadi explicitly stipulates the expense as a debt upon the owner.

Even if a finder has the qadi's permission to spend, can he always claim back his expenses from the owner? The passage explains that the finder's right to reimbursement depends on an additional condition: the qadi must explicitly stipulate that the expense is a debt (dayn) upon the owner. This lesson examines this condition, the reasoning behind it, and the school's most correct narration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key statement
The passage says: 'and his statement in the book (al-Hidayah) 'and he made the expense a debt upon its owner' is an indication that he can only claim from the owner after he appears and the luqatah has not been sold, provided the qadi stipulated the claim upon the owner.'
This is additional to the requirement of evidence.
2
Understand the condition
The finder can only claim reimbursement from the owner if the qadi explicitly stipulated that the expense is a debt (deyn) upon the owner. Without this stipulation, the expense is considered a voluntary donation by the finder.
The stipulation is a condition (shart) for enforceability.
3
Examine the ikhtilaf
The text mentions 'this is one narration, and it is the most correct (al-asahh).' This implies there is another narration that does not require such stipulation.
The asahh view is that stipulation is necessary.
4
Apply the ruling
In practice, a qadi who intends to guarantee reimbursement must use specific words, e.g., 'I order you to spend, and the expense is a debt upon the owner.'
Mere permission to spend is insufficient.

فَلَا بُدَّ مِنَ الْبَيِّنَةِ لِكَشْفِ الْحَالِ وَلَيْسَتِ الْبَيِّنَةُ تُقَامُ لِلْقَضَاءِ وَإِنْ قَالَ لَاَيّنَةَ لِى يَقُوْلُ الْقَاضِي لَهُ أَنْفِقُ عَلَيْهِ إِنْ كُنتَ صَادِقَا فِيمَا قُلْتَ حَتَّى تَرْجِعَ عَلَى الْمَالِكِ إِنْ كَانَ صَادِقًا وَلَا يَرْجِعُ إِنْ كَانَ غَاصِبًا وَقَوْلُهُ فِي الْكِتَابِ وَجَعَلَ النَفَقَةَ دَيْنًا عَلَى صَاحِبِهَا إِشَارَةُ إِلَى أَنَّهُ إِنَّمَا يَرْجِعُ عَلَى الْمَالِكِ بَعْدَ مَا حَضَرَ وَلَمْ تَبِعِ اللَّقْطَةَ إِذَا شَرَطَ الْقَاضِى الرَّجُوعَ عَلَى الْمَالِكِ وَهَذِهِ رِوَايَةً وَهُوَ الْأَصَحُ ترجمہ اور اگر حاکم کے نزدیک یہی بات بہتر ہو کہ اس جانور کو نفقہ ( دانہ یا چارہ ) دیا جائے تو اس ملتقط کو اس بات کی اجازت دے دے اور اس کے خرچ کو اس کے مالک کے ذمہ قرض قرار دے دے ( یعنی بطور قرض اس پر خرچ کرتا رہے کیونکہ حاکم کو ہر ایک پر نظر رکھنے کا حکم ہے۔ اور مذکورہ انتظام ہی میں اصل مالک اور اس ملتقط پر بہتری کی نظر ہوگی۔ اس موقع میں مشائخ رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ حاکم ملتقط کو صرف دو یا تین دن جو مناسب سمجھے دانہ اور چارہ دینے کا حکم اور اگر صرف خرچ کرنے کے لئے تو کہا مگر مالک پر اسے قرض ہونے کی شرط نہیں کی ہو تو اس سے واپس نہیں مانگ سکتا ہے)۔ تشریح ملحق شخص جانور کو قاضی کے سامنے پیش کرے گا قاضی دو تین دن تک جانور پر خرچ کرنے کا سے لے لینے کا اختیار رکھتا ہے جبکہ قاضی نے نفقہ کیلئے قرض کی شرط لگائی ہے ۔
He said: In al-Asl, Imam Muhammad stipulated establishing evidence, and this is correct, because it is possible that it may be a usurpation in his hand, and he does not order spending on it; rather, he only orders spending in the case of a trust. So evidence is necessary to reveal the situation, and the evidence is not established for the sake of judicial ruling. And if he says 'I have no evidence,' the qadi says to him: 'Spend on it if you are truthful in what you say, so that you may claim reimbursement from the owner if you are truthful, and you cannot claim if you are a usurper.' And his statement in the book (al-Hidayah) 'and he made the expense a debt upon its owner' is an indication that he can only claim from the owner after he appears and the luqatah has not been sold, provided the qadi stipulated the claim upon the owner. And this is one narration, and it is the most correct. ... [Urdu translation and commentary] ... Explanation: The finder will bring the animal before the qadi. The qadi will order spending for two or three days, as there is hope of the owner's appearance; this short period is better for the owner, and there is no benefit in a longer period. Commentary
This passage addresses two important procedural issues from Imam Muhammad's al-Mabsut: the requirement of bayyinah (testimony) and the condition for reimbursement. First, when a person claims to be a finder of a lost animal and seeks qadi's authorization to spend on it, he must produce witnesses that he is indeed a trustee (amin) and not a usurper (ghasib). Imam Muhammad stipulates this as a precaution because the qadi's order to spend is only for amanah, not for a ghasib. The evidence is not for the purpose of a judicial ruling (qada') but to ascertain the truth. If the claimant cannot produce evidence, the qadi says, 'Spend if you are truthful; if you are truthful, you may claim from the owner; if you are a usurper, you cannot claim.' This encourages honesty. Second, the text clarifies that the finder can only claim reimbursement from the owner after the owner appears and the animal has not been sold, and only if the qadi explicitly stipulated that the expense is a debt repayable by the owner. This latter condition is essential; without it, the finder cannot demand repayment. The passage notes that this is the most correct narration (al-asahh) within the Hanafi school. This ruling protects both parties: the owner from unjustified claims, and the honest finder who acted under judicial authority.

Key Terms
أصح (asahh): Most correct; the preferred narration regarding the condition of stipulating reimbursement.
دين (dayn): Debt; the expense is made a debt on the owner through qadi's stipulation.

Key Takeaway

The Judge's Ruling on Expenditure for a Found Animal (Luqatah) and the Condition of Evidence
Ruling on judge ordering spending on luqatah animal with condition of evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which a judge orders spending on a found animal and explain why evidence is required, and identify the mufta bihi position in the intra-Hanafi difference.

Core Idea
A judge may order spending on a found animal only after the finder proves it is a trust, not usurped.

This passage examines the judge's role when a finder brings a lost animal to court. The key issue is whether the judge can order the finder to spend on the animal and under what conditions the finder can reclaim those expenses from the owner. The Hanafi ruling distinguishes between the animal being a trust (amanah) or usurped (ghasb), requiring evidence to resolve the ambiguity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the judicial act
The passage discusses the judge's order (amr) to the finder to spend on the found animal (luqatah). Determine the nature of this order—it is not a direct obligation on the finder but a permission under specific conditions.
The judge only orders spending for a short period (2-3 days) to avoid loss due to prolonged expenditure.
2
Locate the condition
The text states that the judge stipulates the condition of establishing evidence (bayyinah) that the animal is a trust (amanah), not usurped (ghasb). Find this condition in the Arabic: 'wa fi al-asl sharata iqamata al-bayyinati wa huwa al-sahihu'.
The evidence is not for a judicial verdict but to reveal the true situation.
3
Trace the rationale
The judge does not order spending on a usurped item. Since the animal could be either amanah or ghasb, evidence is necessary to determine which applies. This connects to the broader principle that the judge's order is only valid for a trust.
The proof is rational (ma'qul) based on the distinction between wadi'ah and ghasb.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
There is another narration (riwayah) that does not require evidence. The author declares the condition view 'al-ashah' (more correct). Identify this difference and the preferred view.
This ikhtilaf is within the Hanafi school, not between schools.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The mufta bihi (operative position) is that the judge must explicitly stipulate the condition of evidence and also stipulate recourse against the owner for the expenditure to become a debt. Apply this to a real scenario.
The finder cannot automatically claim expenses; it depends on the judge's explicit stipulation.

Source Text

بَابُ اللَّقْطَةِ. يَأْمُرُ بِهَا لِأَنَّ دَارَةَ التَّفَقَةِ [؟] مُسْتَأْصِلَةٌ فَلَا نَظَرَ فِي الْإِنْفَاقِ مُدَّةً مَدِيدَةً. قَالَ: وَفِي الْأَصْلِ شَرَطَ إِقَامَةَ الْبَيِّنَةِ وَهُوَ الصَّحِيحُ لِأَنَّهُ يَحْتَمِلُ أَنْ يَكُونَ غَصْبًا فِي يَدِهِ وَلَا يَأْمُرُ فِيهِ بِالْإِنْفَاقِ وَإِنَّمَا يَأْمُرُ بِهِ فِي الْوَدِيعَةِ فَلَا بُدَّ مِنَ الْبَيِّنَةِ لِكَشْفِ الْحَالِ وَلَيْسَتِ الْبَيِّنَةُ تُقَامُ لِلْقَضَاءِ. وَإِنْ قَالَ لَا بَيِّنَةَ لِي يَقُولُ الْقَاضِي لَهُ: أَنْفِقْ عَلَيْهِ إِنْ كُنْتَ صَادِقًا فِيمَا قُلْتَ حَتَّى تَرْجِعَ عَلَى الْمَالِكِ إِنْ كَانَ صَادِقًا وَلَا يَرْجِعُ إِنْ كَانَ غَاصِبًا. وَقَوْلُهُ فِي الْكِتَابِ: وَجَعَلَ النَّفَقَةَ دَيْنًا عَلَى صَاحِبِهَا إِشَارَةٌ إِلَى أَنَّهُ إِنَّمَا يَرْجِعُ عَلَى الْمَالِكِ بَعْدَ مَا حَضَرَ وَلَمْ تَبِعِ اللَّقْطَةُ إِذَا شَرَطَ الْقَاضِي الرُّجُوعَ عَلَى الْمَالِكِ. وَهَذِهِ رِوَايَةٌ وَهُوَ الْأَصَحُ.
Chapter of Luqatah. He orders spending on it because the [؟] of expenditure is exhaustive, so there is no consideration for spending for a long period. He said: In Al-Asl, he stipulated the establishment of evidence, and that is the correct view, because it is possible that it is a usurpation in his hand, and he does not order spending in that case; rather he orders it in the case of a deposit. So evidence is necessary to reveal the situation, and the evidence is not established for the purpose of a judicial verdict. If he says, 'I have no evidence,' the judge says to him: 'Spend on it if you are truthful in what you said, so that you may claim repayment from the owner if he is truthful, and he will not claim if he is a usurper.' His statement in the book: 'And he made the expenditure a debt upon its owner' is an indication that he only claims repayment from the owner after he has appeared and the found animal has not been sold, if the judge stipulated the repayment from the owner. This is a narration and it is the more correct.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Luqatah discusses the judge's role when a finder brings a found animal to court. The judge may order the finder to spend on the animal for a short period (two or three days) because prolonged expenditure would lead to loss. However, Imam Muhammad in his book Al-Asl stipulated that the finder must establish evidence (bayyinah) that the animal is a trust (amanah) in his hand, not usurped (ghasb). This is the correct position because if it were usurped, the judge would not order spending. Evidence is needed to reveal the true situation. The evidence is not for the purpose of a judicial verdict against a defendant; rather it is to prove the nature of the possession. If the finder has no evidence, the judge tells him to spend voluntarily, but he can only reclaim the expense from the owner if he is truthful and the judge had stipulated repayment. If the finder is a usurper, he cannot reclaim. The ruling that the judge makes the expenditure a debt on the owner is valid only if the judge explicitly stipulated the right of recourse against the owner. This is the more authentic narration (al-ashah).

Key Terms
اللقطة (al-luqatah): A lost property found by someone, specifically an animal in this context.
الوديعة (al-wadīʿah): A deposit or trust; the animal is considered a wadi'ah if the finder took it as an amanah.
الغصب (al-ghaṣb): Usurpation; taking property illegally, which precludes the judge's order for expenditure.
البينة (al-bayyinah): Evidence or proof, here meaning witnesses to establish that the animal is a trust, not usurped.
النفقة (al-nafaqah): Expenditure on the animal's feed and care.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad's correct view in Al-Asl, what must the finder establish for the judge to order spending on a found animal with the right of recourse against the owner?
A) The finder must be willing to pay for the animal's feed himself.
B) The finder must establish evidence (bayyinah) that the animal is a trust (amanah), not usurped.
C) The finder must have known the owner's identity before bringing the animal to court.
D) The finder must have fed the animal for at least one year before approaching the judge.

Key Takeaway
The judge's order to spend on a found animal requires the finder to prove it is a trust (amanah) and the judge to explicitly stipulate repayment from the owner for the expenditure to become a debt.

Luqatah — Found Property
intermediate
8 min
Finder's Right to Withhold Until Expenses Paid
Ruling on finder's right to withhold until expenses reimbursed, with analogy to rahn.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a finder's right to withhold a found item, apply the qiyas to the returner of a runaway slave, and explain the effect of the item perishing before and after withholding.

Core Idea
The finder may withhold the found item as security for expenses; after withholding, it is like a pledge and the debt falls if the item perishes.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a practical question in the law of luqatah: can the finder refuse to hand over the item until the owner reimburses expenses? The Hanafi school answers yes, drawing an analogy to the returner of a runaway slave and to the law of pledge (rahn). Understanding this ruling clarifies the finder's rights and the consequences if the item is lost.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage states that when the owner comes, the finder has the right to withhold the item until the owner brings the expenses.
2
Locate the proof – Qiyas
The author provides an analogy: just as the returner of a runaway slave may detain the slave for his reward, so may the finder withhold the item.
The asl (original case) is the returner's right to detain.
3
Trace the illa (effective cause)
The finder revived the item with his expenditure, creating a security right similar to the returner's right to detain for the reward.
The illa is the expenditure that 'revives' the item.
4
Note the consequence – Perishing
If the item perishes before the finder withholds, the debt of expenses remains; if after withholding, the debt falls because the item becomes like a pledge (rahn).
After habs, the item is treated as a rahn; loss without negligence cancels the debt.
5
Recognize cross-madhhab dispute
Malik and Shafi'i hold that the finder must hand over the item upon request without withholding, whereas Hanafis allow withholding.
The difference stems from viewing the finder as a mere depositary versus a party with a security interest.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ فَإِذَا حَضَرَ يَعْنِى الْمَالِكُ فَلِلْمُلْتَقِطِ أَنْ يَسْتَعَهَا مِنْهُ حَتَّى يَحْضُرَ النَّفَقَةَ لِأَنَّهُ يُحْيِي بِنَفَقَتِهِ فَصَارَ كَأَنَّهُ اسْتَفَادَ الْمِلْكَ مِنْ جِهَتِهِ فَأَشْهَرَ الْمَبِيعَ [؟] وَأَقْرَبُ مِنْ ذَلِكَ رَادُّ الآبِقِ فَإِنَّ لَهُ الْحَبْسَ لاسْتِيفَاءِ الْجُعْلِ لِمَا ذَكَرْنَا ثُمَّ لا يَسْقُطُ دَيْنُ النَّفَقَةِ بِهَلَاكِ فِي يَدِ الْمُلْتَقِطِ قَبْلَ الْحَبْسِ وَيَسْقُطُ إِذَا هَلَكَ بَعْدَ الْحَبْسِ لِأَنَّهُ يَصِيرُ بِالْحَبْسِ شَبِيهَ الرَّهْنِ
He said: When the owner comes, the finder has the right to withhold the item from him until he brings the expenses, because the finder revived it with his expenditure, so it is as if he acquired ownership from him and made the sale public. Closer to that is the returner of a runaway slave: he has the right to detain him for collecting the reward, for what we mentioned. Then the debt of the expenses does not fall if the item perishes in the finder's hand before the withholding, but it falls if it perishes after the withholding, because by the withholding it becomes similar to a pledge.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It establishes the Hanafi position that a finder (multaqit) may withhold the found item from the owner until the owner reimburses the finder's expenses (nafaqa). The proof is by analogy (qiyas): just as a person who captures and returns a runaway slave may detain him as security for his reward, and just as a creditor may hold a pledged item (rahn) as security for a debt, so too the finder may withhold the item. The passage further explains the consequence if the found item perishes: before the finder exercises the right of withholding (habs), the debt of expenses remains; after withholding, the debt falls off because the item becomes like a pledge—if it perishes in the pledgee's hands without negligence, the debt is canceled.

Key Terms
الْحَبْس (al-habs): The act of withholding the found item from the owner as a security for expenses.
الرَّهْن (ar-rahn): A pledge left as security for a debt; if it perishes without the pledgee's fault, the debt is canceled.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a found item perishes in the finder's hand AFTER he has withheld it from the owner, what happens to the finder's debt of expenses?
A) The debt remains and must be paid by the owner.
B) The debt falls and the finder loses his claim.
C) The finder becomes the owner of the item.
D) The finder must pay compensation to the owner.

Key Takeaway
The finder may withhold the found item for expenses; after withholding, the item is treated as a pledge and the debt falls if it perishes without negligence.
